(a)  Nothing in this Code, or the resolution or ordinance adopting this Code, shall be construed to repeal or otherwise affect the validity of any of the following: 
(1)  Any offense or act committed or done, or any penalty or forfeiture incurred, or any contract or right established or accruing before the effective date of this Code. 
(2)  Any resolution or ordinance promising or guaranteeing the payment of money for the county, or authorizing the issuance of any bonds of the county, or any evidence of the county's indebtedness. 
(3)  Any contract or obligation assumed by the county. 
(4)  Any resolution or ordinance fixing the salary of any county officer or employee. 
(5)  Any right or franchise granted by the county. 
(6)  Any resolution or ordinance dedicating, naming, establishing, locating, relocating, opening, widening, paving, etc., any street or public way in the county. 
(7)  Any appropriation resolution or ordinance. 
(8)  Any resolution or ordinance which, by its own terms, is effective for a stated or limited term. 
(9)  Any resolution or ordinance providing for local improvements and assessing taxes for such local improvements. 
(10)  Any zoning resolution or ordinance. 
(11)  Any resolution or ordinance dedicating or accepting any subdivision plat. 
(12)  Any resolution or ordinance describing or altering the boundaries of the county. 
(13)  The administrative resolutions or ordinances of the county not in conflict or inconsistent with the provisions of this Code. 
(14)  Any resolution or ordinance levying or imposing taxes not included in this Code. 
(15)  Any resolution or ordinance establishing or prescribing street grades in the county. 
(b)  No such resolution or ordinance shall be construed to revive any resolution or ordinance or part thereof that has been repealed by a subsequent resolution or ordinance which is repealed by this chapter. All such resolutions or ordinances are recognized as continuing in full force and effect to the same extent as if set out at length in this Code. 
Sec. 1-14. - Provisions considered continuations of existing resolutions. 
The provisions appearing in this Code, so far as they are the same as resolutions or ordinances adopted prior to this Code and included in such Code, shall be considered as continuations thereof and not as new enactments. 
Sec. 1-15. - Severability of parts of Code. 
It is declared to be the intention of the board of commissioners that the sections, paragraphs, sentences, clauses and phrases of this Code are severable, and if any phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph or section of this Code shall be declared unconstitutional by the valid judgment or decree of any court of competent jurisdiction, such unconstitutionality shall not affect any of the remaining phrases, clauses, sentences, paragraphs and sections of this Code, since they would have been enacted by the board of commissioners without the incorporation in the Code of any such unconstitutional phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph or section. 
State Law reference— Severability, O.C.G.A. § 1-1-3. 
Sec. 1-16. - Amendments to Code. 
(a)  All resolutions or ordinances passed subsequent to this Code which amend, repeal or in any way affect this Code, may be numbered in accordance with the numbering system of this Code and printed for inclusion in this Code. In the case of repealed chapters, sections and subsections, or any part thereof, by subsequent resolutions or ordinances, such repealed portions may be excluded from the Code by omission from reprinted pages affected thereby. The subsequent resolutions or ordinances as numbered and printed or omitted, in the case of repeal, shall be prima facie evidence of such subsequent resolutions or ordinances until such time that this Code and subsequent resolutions or ordinances numbered or omitted are readopted as a new Code by the board of commissioners. 
(b)  Amendments to any of the provisions of this Code may be made by amending such provisions by specific reference to the section number of this Code. 
(c)  If a new section not previously existing in the Code is to be added, the following language may be used: "That the Code of Ordinances, Dade County, Georgia, is amended by adding a section (or article or chapter) to be numbered, which section shall read as follows: . . . ." The new section may then be set out in full as desired. 
(d)  All sections, articles, chapters or provisions desired to be repealed should be specifically repealed by section, article or chapter number, as the case may be. 
Sec. 1-17. - Supplementation of Code. 
(a)  By contract or by county personnel, supplements to this Code shall be prepared at least on an annual basis. A supplement to the Code shall include all substantive, permanent and general parts of resolutions or ordinances passed by the board of commissioners during the period covered by the supplement and all changes made thereby in the Code. The pages of a supplement shall be so numbered that they will fit properly into the Code and will, where necessary, replace pages which have become obsolete or partially obsolete, and the new pages shall be so prepared that, when they have been inserted, the Code will be current through the date of the adoption of the latest resolution or ordinance included in the supplement. 
(b)  In preparing a supplement to this Code, all portions of the Code which have been repealed shall be excluded from the Code by the omission thereof from reprinted pages. 
(c)  When preparing a supplement to this Code, the codifier (meaning the person authorized to prepare the supplement) may make formal, nonsubstantive changes in resolutions and parts of resolutions included in the supplement, insofar as it is necessary to do so to embody them into a unified Code. For example, the codifier may: 
(1)  Organize the resolution or ordinance material into appropriate subdivisions. 
(2)  Provide appropriate catchlines, headings and titles for sections and other subdivisions of the Code printed in the supplement, and make changes in such catchlines, headings and titles. 
(3)  Assign appropriate numbers to sections and other subdivisions to be inserted in the Code and, where necessary to accommodate new material, change existing section or other subdivision numbers. 
(4)  Change the words "this resolution" or words of the same meaning to "this chapter," "this article," "this division," etc., as the case may be, or to "sections ________ to ________" (inserting section numbers to indicate the sections of the Code which embody the substantive sections of the resolution or ordinance incorporated into the Code). 
(5)  Make other nonsubstantive changes necessary to preserve the original meanings of resolution or ordinance sections inserted into the Code; but in no case shall the codifier make any change in the meaning or effect of resolution material included in the supplement or already embodied in the Code. 
Sec. 1-18. - Altering Code. 
It shall be unlawful for any person in the county to change or amend by additions or deletions any part or portion of this Code, or to insert or delete pages, or portions thereof, or to alter or tamper with such Code in any manner whatsoever which will cause the law of the county to be misrepresented thereby, unless so authorized by resolution or ordinance or other official act of the board of commissioners. Any person violating this section shall be punished as provided in section 1-19. 
State Law reference— Altering, falsifying or stealing public records unlawful, O.C.G.A. § 45-11-1. 
Sec. 1-19. - General penalty, continuing violations; authority granted to court. 
(a)  For the purpose of protecting and preserving the public health, safety and welfare, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-20 gives the board of commissioners authorization to adopt resolutions and ordinances for the governing and policing of the unincorporated areas of the county, violations of which resolutions and ordinances may be punished by fine and/or imprisonment. 
(b)  In 1991 the Georgia General Assembly amended O.C.G.A. § 36-1-20, relating to resolutions and ordinances for governing and policing unincorporated areas of the county, so as to increase the maximum fine from five hundred dollars ($500.00) to one thousand dollars ($1,000.00). 
(c)  O.C.G.A. § 36-1-20 gives jurisdiction over violations of county resolutions and ordinances to the magistrate court of the county. 
(d)  O.C.G.A. § 36-1-20 is incorporated as a part of the Code of Ordinances, Dade County, Georgia. 
(e)  Whenever in this Code, or in any resolution or ordinance of the county, any act is prohibited or is made or declared to be unlawful or an offense, or whenever in this Code, or any resolution or ordinance, the doing of an act is required and the failure to do such act is declared to be unlawful, and no specific penalty is provided, and unless otherwise provided by state law, the violation of any such provision of this Code or any such resolution or ordinance shall be punished by a fine not to exceed one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) and imprisonment in the county prison or in the county jail and work and labor on the streets or public works of the county, whether within or without the corporate limits, not exceeding one hundred eighty (180) days or both a fine and sentence of imprisonment and labor and all sentences may be in the alternative and fines may be imposed with the alternative of sentence to imprisonment and labor, if the fines are not paid. Each day any violation of this Code or of any resolution or ordinance shall continue shall constitute a separate offense. 
(f)  The judge of the magistrate court shall have the power and authority to: 
(1)  Impose upon persons convicted in the magistrate court the fines provided for in this Code, the resolutions and ordinances of the county, or as otherwise provided by law, with the alternative of other punishment allowed by law, if such fines are not paid; 
(2)  Sentence such person to community service work; or 
(3)  Impose a sentence consisting of any combination of the penalties provided for in this section. 
(g)  The judge of the magistrate court shall have full power and authority to declare the forfeiture of bonds given by offenders for their appearance before the court upon the offender's failure to appear as provided for in such bond. The procedure for the forfeiture of such bonds shall be as is provided for the forfeiture of bonds and recognizance set forth in O.C.G.A. § 17-6-70 et seq. 
State Law reference— Imposition of additional penalty for certain drug offenses, O.C.G.A. § 15-21-100; imposition of additional penalty for offense of driving under the influence of alcohol or drugs, O.C.G.A. § 15-21-112; additional penalty assessments for jail construction and staffing, O.C.G.A. § 15-21-93; punishment for misdemeanors generally, O.C.G.A. § 17-10-3; deposit of driver's license for violations of laws pertaining to traffic and motor vehicles, O.C.G.A. § 17-6-11; payments to peace officers' annuity and benefit fund from revenues collected from fines and fees, O.C.G.A. § 47-17-60 et seq.; alternative punishments for violations involving a traffic offense, O.C.G.A. § 17-10-3(e). 
Sec. 1-20. - Liability for violations by corporations and other associations. 
(a)  Any violation of this Code by any officer, agent or other person acting for or employed by any corporation or unincorporated association or organization, while acting within the scope of his office or employment, shall in every case also be deemed to be a violation by such corporation, association or organization. 
(b)  Any officer, agent or other person acting for or employed by any corporation or unincorporated association or organization shall be subject and liable to punishment as well as such corporation or unincorporated association or organization for the violation by it of any provisions of this Code, where such violation was the act or omission, or the result of the act, omission or order of any such person. 
Sec. 1-21. - Designation of District Attorney's Office of the Lookout Mountain Judicial Circuit to prosecute criminal offenses. 
The board of commissioners hereby designates the District Attorney's Office of the Lookout Mountain Judicial Circuit to prosecute all misdemeanor criminal offenses within the jurisdiction of the magistrate court of the county pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 15-10-262. 
(Res. No. R-16-00, 11-2-2000) 
Chapter 2 - ADMINISTRATION[1]

Cross reference— The administrative resolutions or ordinances of the county not in conflict or inconsistent with the provisions of this Code saved from repeal, § 1-13(13); civil emergencies, ch. 22; administration of flood control regulations, § 26-46 et seq.; administration and application of road addressing regulations, § 38-67; taxation, ch. 50. 
State Law reference— Claims against counties, O.C.G.A. § 36-11-1 et seq.; local government zoning powers, O.C.G.A. § 36-66-2; provisions applicable to counties and municipal corporations, O.C.G.A. § 36-80-1 et seq.; home rule for counties, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ I; supplemental powers of municipalities and counties enumerated, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 2-1. - Regulations governing use of county vehicles. 
The following regulations governing the use and operation of county-owned or county-leased vehicles shall be established: 
(1)  There shall be placed on the front doors of both sides of county vehicles a sticker or other markings identifying the vehicle as being owned by the county. 
(2)  There shall be no smoking of any tobacco products permitted in county vehicles. 
(3)  County vehicles may be driven home only by those county employees who could reasonably be expected to provide emergency services after regular work hours. These employees shall include the 911 director, the director of public works, road supervisors, and such other employees as may be designated by the county commission. 
(4)  It is expressly understood and intended that the regulations set forth in this section apply to all vehicles owned or leased by the county, but not for those vehicles assigned by the county commission exclusively for use by the sheriff's department. 
(Res. R-03-07, 1-8-2007) 
Sec. 2-2. - Smoking or other use of tobacco products on county property and vehicles. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
County facility. Any building, office complex, office center, courthouse, civic center, auditorium, jail, or other enclosed structure, owned or otherwise under the exclusive control of the county. There is specifically included within this definition all county property within fifty (50) feet of the building or enclosed structure. 
County vehicle. Any automobile, truck, van, or other motor vehicle designed primarily for on the road use and which is owned or otherwise under the exclusive control of the county. 
Smoking. The burning of any tobacco product in a cigarette, cigar, or pipe of any type or kind. 
Tobacco products. Any kind or type of tobacco, whether loose leaf, processed, or rolled, that is intended, packaged, or sold for the purpose of chewing, dipping, or smoking. 
(b)  Prohibited acts. It shall be unlawful for any person to smoke or to otherwise use tobacco products in county facilities or county vehicles. Except, however, the Dade County Sheriff is authorized to designate one (1) or more specific locations within the confinement area of the county jail as a tobacco use area. Nothing in this section shall be construed to authorize tobacco use in any areas of the county jail accessible to members of the general public. 
(c)  Violation; penalties. In addition to penalties which may be imposed under state law for the violation of O.C.G.A § 16-12-2, any violation of the provisions of this section shall constitute a misdemeanor and shall be punishable by penalties and costs as set forth in section 1-19 of this Code. 
(Ord. No. 12-01-11, §§ 1—3, 12-1-2011) 
Secs. 2-3—2-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Any resolution or ordinance fixing the salary of any county officer or employee saved from repeal, § 1-13(4). 
State Law reference— Employment of additional temporary personnel and equipment for assistance of county officers or departments, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-11; civil service system for county employees authorized, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ I; O.C.G.A. § 36-1-21; county manager authorized, O.C.G.A. § 36-5-22; code of ethics for government service, O.C.G.A. § 45-10-1; fair Employment Practices Act of 1978, O.C.G.A. § 45-19-20 et seq. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-31. - Personnel provisions not affected by Code. 
Nothing in this Code or in the ordinance adopting this Code shall affect any ordinance relating to the city's personnel classification system, employee pay plan, retirement plan or employee benefits, including, but not limited to, Resolution R-8-97, effective July 1, 1997, adopting the Dade County Personnel Policies. All such ordinances are recognized as continuing in full force and effect to the same extent as if set out in full in this Code. 
State Law reference— Social security coverage for employees of the state and political subdivisions of the state, O.C.G.A. § 47-18-1 et seq. 
Sec. 2-32. - Workers' compensation coverage—Elected officials. 
Certain elected officials of the county shall be covered under the Association of County Commissioners of Georgia Group Self-Insured Workers' Compensation Fund. While performing their elected duties, the county commissioner, sheriff, probate judge, clerk of the court, magistrate judge, tax-commissioner and coroner shall be covered under the worker's compensation laws of the state. 
(Res. of 2-18-1992(1), § I) 
Sec. 2-33. - Workers' compensation coverage—Volunteer firefighters, emergency medical technicians, rescue workers. 
Volunteer firefighters, emergency medical technicians and rescue workers of the county shall be covered under the Association of County Commissioners of Georgia Group Self-Insured Workers' Compensation Fund. While performing their duties, such workers shall be covered under the worker's compensation laws of the state. 
(Res. of 2-18-1992(2), § I) 
Sec. 2-34. - County issued government purchasing cards and credit cards. 
(a)  Intent and scope. This section is intended to comply with the policy requirements of O.C.G.A. § 36-80-24 regarding the use of county issued government purchasing cards and credit cards. 
(b)  Definitions. [The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:] 
Authorized elected official means an elected official designated by public vote of the board of commissioners to receive a county issued government purchasing card or credit card. 
Card administrator means the purchasing card and credit card administrator designated by the Dade County Board of Commissioners. 
County means Dade County and/or the board of commissioners. 
County purchase card, county p-card or county credit card means a financial transaction card issued by any business organization, financial institution, or any duly authorized agent of such organization or institution, used by a county official to purchase goods, services and other things of value on behalf of the county. 
Financial transaction card means an instrument or device as the term is defined in O.C.G.A. § 16-9-30(5). 
User agreement means the required agreement between the board of commissioners and the authorized elected officials which restricts the use of a county purchasing card or credit card. 
(c)  Designated elected officials. The Dade County Board of Commissioners ("county"), in its discretion, may authorize specific county elected officials to use a county purchasing card or credit card by adoption of a resolution in a public meeting. 
No authorized elected official may use a county purchasing card or credit card until and unless he or she has executed the county's purchasing card and credit card user agreement. 
The county will not make payments to any business organization, financial institution, or any duly authorized agent of such organization or institution, for amounts charged by an elected official to any purchasing cards or credit cards that are not issued pursuant to this section or for any purchases that are not authorized by this section. 
(d)  Card administrator. The board of commissioners shall designate a county purchasing card and credit card administrator. The responsibilities of the card administrator include: 
(1)  Manage county issued purchasing cards and credit cards. 
(2)  Serve as the main point of contact for all county purchasing card and credit card issues. 
(3)  Serve as liaison to the elected officials authorized to use a purchasing card or credit card and their staff, as well as to the issuer of the purchasing card or credit card. 
(4)  Provide training on card policies and procedures to the elected officials authorized to use a purchasing card or credit card and their staff. 
(5)  Develop internal procedures to ensure timely payment of cards. 
(6)  Assist authorized elected officials to dispute transactions when necessary. 
(7)  Establish internal procedures to ensure compliance with this section, county procurement ordinances and policies, county purchasing card and credit card user agreements, applicable agreements with the business organization, financial institution, or any duly authorized agent of such organization or institution, issuing card, and state law, specifically, O.C.G.A. §§ 16-9-37 and 36-80-24. 
(8)  Document internal controls, audits and other measures to prevent and detect misuse or abuse of the cards. 
(9)  Audit and reconcile transactions monthly. 
(10)  Maintain records for at least seven years or as otherwise provided by the county's record retention policy. 
(e)  Use of cards . 
(1)  Authorized purchases. County purchase cards and credit cards may be used to purchase goods and services directly related to the public duties of the authorized elected official only. All purchases are subject to the terms of this section, the county purchasing card and credit card user agreement, county procurement policies and ordinances, and the adopted budget. 
Only authorized elected officials may use a county purchase card or credit card for purchases or payments. The cards, and use of the cards, are not transferrable to employees. The authorized elected official shall use care to ensure that others do not have access to the card account number, expiration date and security code. 
Unless otherwise approved by the governing authority or established in the county purchasing card and credit card user agreement, the transaction limits are as follows: 
Per transaction: $3,000.00 
Per month: $5,000.00 
(2)  Unauthorized purchases. County purchasing cards and credit cards shall not be used for goods and services not directly related to the official responsibilities of the authorized elected official. Additionally, cards shall not be used to avoid compliance with the county's purchasing ordinances and procedures, to purchase goods and services that are not approved in the county's budget, to purchase goods and services exceeding the per transaction or per month limit, or to make purchases not in compliance with the county purchasing card and credit card user agreement. 
(3)  Receipts and documentation. Receipts, invoices and other supporting documentation of all purchases made with a county purchasing card or credit card shall be obtained and maintained by the authorized county elected official for five years or as otherwise provided by the county's record retention policy. If an original or duplicate cannot be produced, a sworn affidavit of the authorized elected official may be substituted. The documentation must include the supplier or merchant information (i.e., name and location), quantity, description, unit price, total price, price paid without sales tax and an explanation of the purchase sufficient to show that the expense was in the performance of official county duties. 
(4)  Public records. All receipt and other documentation of purchases are public records and subject to the requirements of O.C.G.A. § 50-18-70 et seq. 
(f)  Review of purchases and audit. Proper documentation of purchases, internal controls and other measures prevent and allow detection to misuse or abuse of county issued purchase cards and credit cards. Authorized elected officials and staff that process payments under this program shall cooperate and comply with the procedures established by the county. 
(1)  Review of purchases. All purchases shall be reviewed according to the Dade County's Accounting Department Policy and Procedure Manual (credit card section) as may be amended from time to time. 
(2)  Audits. The card administrator shall perform an annual review of the card program to ensure adequacy of internal policies and procedures, cardholder spending limits, monthly reconciliation procedures and documentation for transactions. Elected officials and staff shall cooperate with such review. 
(g)  Violations. 
(1)  An elected official shall reimburse the county for any purchases made with a county issued purchase card or credit card in violation of this section or the user agreement. 
(2)  In the discretion of the county governing authority, failure to comply with the procedures outlined in this section may result in: 
a.  A warning; 
b.  Suspension of the elected official's authority to use a county purchase card or credit card; or 
c.  Revocation of the elected official's authority to use a county purchase card or credit card. 
(3)  Nothing in this section shall preclude the county governing authority from referring misuse of a purchase card or credit card for prosecution to the appropriate authorities. 
( Ord. No. 02-04-16 , § I—VII, 2-4-2016) 
Secs. 2-35—2-55. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - DRUG AND ALCOHOL TESTING[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, ch. 6. 

Sec. 2-56. - Policy. 
The county board of commissioners is dedicated to the providing of safe, dependable and economical services to the citizens of the county. County employees are our most valuable resource and it is goal of the board of commissioners to provide a healthy, satisfying work environment which promotes personal opportunities for growth. In meeting these goals, it shall be the policy to: 
(1)  Ensure that employees are not impaired in their ability to perform assigned duties in a safe, productive and healthy manner; 
(2)  Create a work place environment free from the adverse effects of drug abuse and alcohol misuse; 
(3)  Prohibit the unlawful manufacture, distribution, dispensing, possession or use of controlled substances; and 
(4)  Encourage employees to seek professional assistance any time personal problems, including alcohol or drug dependency, adversely affects their ability to perform their assigned duties. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 1.0, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-57. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this division is to ensure worker fitness for duty and to protect county employees, passengers and the public from the risks posed by the misuse of alcohol and use of prohibited drugs. This division is also intended to comply with all applicable federal regulations governing workplace antidrug and alcohol programs in the transit industry. The Federal Transit Administration (FTA) of the U.S. Department of Transportation (DOT) has published 49 CFR 653 and 49 CFR 654, as amended, that mandate urine drug testing and breath alcohol testing for safety-sensitive positions and prohibits performance of safety-sensitive functions when there is a positive test result. The U.S. Department of Transportation has also published 49 CFR 40, as amended, that sets standards for the collection and testing of urine and breath specimens. In addition, the federal government published 49 CFR 29, The Drug-Free Workplace Act of 1988, which requires the establishment of drug-free workplace policies and the reporting of certain drug-related offenses to the Federal Transit Administration. This policy incorporates those requirements for safety-sensitive employees and others, when so noted. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 2.0, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-58. - Applicability. 
This division applies to all safety-sensitive employees and contractors when they are on county property or when performing any county-related safety-sensitive business. This division applies to off-site lunch periods or breaks when an employee is scheduled to return to work. A "safety-sensitive" function means any duty related to the safe operation of any county transportation service, including the operation of a vehicle, dispatch or maintenance of a vehicle or equipment used in transportation services, personnel who carry firearms, equipment operation, equipment maintenance, emergency personnel, emergency dispatch operations and any other employee who holds a commercial driver's license. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 3.0, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-59. - Proper application of policy. 
The county is dedicated to ensuring fair and equitable application of this division. Supervisors/managers are therefor required to use and apply all aspects of this division in an unbiased and impartial manner. Any supervisor/manager who knowingly disregards the requirements of this division, or who is found to deliberately misuse this division in regard to subordinates, shall be subject to disciplinary action, up to and including termination of employment. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 5.7, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-60. - Prohibited substances. 
Prohibited substances addressed by this division include the following: 
(1)  Illegally used controlled substances or drugs. The use of any illegal drug or any substance identified in schedules I—V of section 202 of the Controlled Substance Act (21 USC § 812), as further defined by 21 CFR 1300.11—1300.15, is prohibited at all times unless a legal prescription has been written for the substance. This includes, but is not limited to, marijuana, amphetamines, opiates, phencyclidine (PCP) and cocaine, as well as any drug not approved for medical use by the U.S. Drug Administration. The term "illegal use" includes use of any illegal drug, misuse of legally prescribed drugs and use of illegally obtained prescription drugs. 
(2)  Legal drugs. The appropriate use of legally prescribed drugs and nonprescription medications is not prohibited; however, the use of any substance which carries a warning label that indicates that mental function, motor skills or judgment may be adversely affected by use of such substance must be reported to a county supervisor. The employee must obtain a written release from the attending physician releasing the person to perform his job duties any time such employee obtains a performance-altering prescription. A "legally prescribed drug" means an individual has a prescription or other written approval from a physician for the use of a drug in the course of medical treatment. Such prescription or written approval must include the patient's name, the name of the substance, quantity/amount to be taken and the period of authorization for use of such substance. The misuse or abuse of legal drugs while performing county business is prohibited. 
(3)  Alcohol. The use of beverages containing alcohol or substances including any medication, mouthwash, food, candy or any other substance so that alcohol is present in the body while performing county business is prohibited. The concentration of alcohol is expressed in terms of alcohol per two hundred ten (210) liters of breath as measured by a breath testing device approved for evidentiary purposes. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, §§ 4.0—4.3, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-61. - Prohibited conduct. 
County employees, contract employees and subcontractors are prohibited from engaging in the unlawful manufacture, distribution, dispensing, possession or use of prohibited substances while on county premises, in county vehicles, in uniform or on county business. Employees who violate this section will be discharged from employment. Law enforcement shall be notified, as appropriate, where criminal activity is suspected. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 5.1, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-62. - Intoxication; under the influence. 
Any safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employee who is reasonably suspected of being intoxicated, impaired, under the influence of a prohibited substance or not fit for duty shall be suspended from his job duties pending an investigation and verification of his condition. Employees found to be under the influence of prohibited substances or who fail to pass a drug or alcohol test shall be removed from duty and discharged from employment. A drug or alcohol test is considered positive if the employee is found to have a quantifiable presence of a prohibited substance in his body above the minimum thresholds defined in 49 CFR 40, as amended. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 5.2, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-63. - Alcohol use. 
No safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employee shall report for duty or remain on duty when his ability to perform assigned safety-sensitive functions is adversely affected by alcohol or when his breath alcohol concentration is 0.04 or greater. No safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employee shall use alcohol while on duty, in uniform, while driving a county vehicle (whether on or off duty), while operating county equipment (whether on or off duty), while performing assigned functions or just before or after performing an assigned function. No safety-sensitive employee shall use alcohol within four (4) hours of reporting for duty, or during the hours that he/she is on call. Violation of this section is prohibited and punishable by disciplinary action up to and including termination of employment. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 5.3, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-64. - Compliance with testing requirements. 
All safety-sensitive employees will be subject to urine drug testing and breath alcohol testing as a condition of employment. Any safety-sensitive employee who refuses to comply with a request for testing shall not be hired or shall be removed from duty and discharged from employment. Any safety-sensitive employee who is suspected of falsifying test results through tampering, contamination, adulteration or substitution will be required to undergo an observed collection. Verification of these actions will result in removal from duty and termination from employment. Refusal to comply with testing can include: 
(1)  An inability to provide a sufficient urine sample, saliva sample or breath sample without a valid medical explanation; and 
(2)  A verbal declaration, obstructive behavior or physical absence resulting in the inability to conduct the test. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 5.4, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-65. - Treatment requirements. 
All employees with a drug or alcohol abuse problem are encouraged to use any available resources for treatment of alcohol misuse and illegal drug use. Under certain circumstances, employees may be required to undergo treatment of substance abuse or alcohol misuse. Any employee who refuses or fails to comply with the county requirements for treatment and after care, as a condition to return to duty, shall be subject to disciplinary action, up to and including termination of employment. The cost of any treatment or rehabilitation services will be paid for directly by the employee or his insurance provider. Employees who make self-referrals (i.e., no management intervention or positive test results) will be allowed to take accumulated sick leave and vacation during such treatment or rehabilitation. Employees that test positive for alcohol misuse or illegal drug use will be referred to the substance abuse program for assessment and be discharged from employment. No treatment opportunities will be afforded to those who test positive for alcohol misuse or illegal drug use. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 5.5, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-66. - Notification of conviction. 
All employees are required to notify the county of any criminal drug statute conviction for a violation occurring in the workplace within five (5) days after such conviction. Failure to comply with this section shall result in disciplinary action up to and including termination of employment. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 5.6, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-67. - Testing process. 
(a)  Analytical urine drug testing and breath testing for alcohol may be conducted when circumstances warrant or as required by federal regulations. All safety-sensitive and nonsafety-sensitive employees shall be subject to drug and alcohol testing prior to employment, for reasonable suspicion and following an accident as set forth in sections 2-70—2-72. Refusal to submit to the test or failure to pass the test will be cause for immediate termination of employment. The employee will be referred to a substance abuse professional but will be discharged from employment. Those employees who perform safety-sensitive functions shall also be subject to testing on a random, unannounced basis. Employees who are subject to the jurisdiction of the Federal Transit System and Federal Highway Administration shall be required to undergo testing required by such departments. 
(b)  Drug and alcohol testing shall be conducted in a manner that assures a high degree of accuracy and reliability and using techniques, equipment and laboratory facilities which have been approved by the U.S. Department of Health and Human Services (DHHS). All testing will be conducted consistent with the procedures set forth in 49 CFR 40, as amended. 
(c)  Drugs that will be tested for include marijuana, cocaine, opiates, amphetamines and phencyclidine. An initial drug screen will be conducted on each urine specimen. For those specimens that are not negative, a confirmatory gas chromatography/mass spectrometry (GCMS) test will be performed. The test will be considered positive if the amounts present are above the minimum thresholds established in 49 CFR 40, as amended. In instances where there is a reason to believe an employee is abusing a substance other than the drugs listed in this subsection, the county reserves the right to test for additional drugs under the county's own authority using standard laboratory testing protocols. 
(d)  Tests for breath alcohol concentration will be conducted utilizing a National Highway Traffic Safety Administration (NHTSA)-approved testing device operated by a trained technician. If the initial test indicates an alcohol concentration of 0.02 or greater, a confirmatory test will be performed using a National Highway Traffic Safety Administration-approved evidential breath testing (EBT) device operated by a trained breath alcohol technician (BAT). A safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employee who has a confirmed alcohol concentration of 0.02 or greater but less than 0.04 will be removed from his position of employment for eight (8) hours unless a retest results in a concentration measure of less than 0.02. The inability of an employee to perform safety-sensitive duties due to an alcohol test result of 0.02 or greater but less than 0.04 will be removed from his position for twenty-four (24) hours unless a retest results in a concentration measure of less than 0.02. The inability of an employee to perform assigned duties due to an alcohol test result of greater than 0.02 but less than 0.04 will be considered an unexcused absence subject to county disciplinary procedures. An alcohol concentration of 0.04 or greater will be considered a positive alcohol test and the employee will be removed from his position of employment, informed of educational rehabilitation programs available and referred to a substance abuse professional for assessment. A positive drug and/or alcohol test will also result in disciplinary action up to and including termination of employment. The county affirms the need to protect individual dignity, privacy and confidentiality throughout the testing process. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 5.8, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-68. - When testing performed. 
Alcohol tests will only be performed immediately before, during or immediately after the performance of safety-sensitive job functions. Drug tests will be performed any time a safety-sensitive employee is on duty. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 6.0, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-69. - Employee requested testing. 
Any safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employee who questions the results of a required drug test under sections 2-70—2-75 may request that the split sample be tested. This test must be conducted by a different U.S. Department of Health and Human Services-certified laboratory. The test must be conducted on the split sample that was provided by the employee at the same time as the original sample. All costs for testing are paid by the employee unless the result of the split sample invalidates the result of the original test. The method of collecting, storing and testing the split sample will be consistent with the procedures set forth in 49 CFR 40, as amended. The employee's request for a split sample test must be made to the medical review officer within seventy-two (72) hours of notice of the original sample verified test result. Requests made after seventy-two (72) hours will only be accepted if the request delay was due to documentable facts that were beyond the control of the employee. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 6.1, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-70. - Pre-employment testing. 
All safety-sensitive and nonsafety-sensitive position applicants shall undergo urine drug testing immediately following the offer of employment or transfer into an assigned safety-sensitive position. Receipt by the county of a negative drug test result is required prior to employment or transfer. Failure of a pre-employment drug test will disqualify an applicant for employment for a period of one hundred twenty (120) days. Evidence of the absence of drug dependency from a substance abuse professional that meets county approval and a negative pre-employment drug test will be required prior to further consideration for employment. The cost for the assessment and any subsequent treatment will be the sole responsibility on the individual tested. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 6.2, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-71. - Reasonable suspicion testing. 
All safety-sensitive and nonsafety-sensitive employees may be subject to a fitness for duty evaluation and urine and/or breath testing when there are reasons to believe that drug or alcohol use is adversely affecting such employee's job performance. A reasonable suspicion referral for testing will be made on the basis of documented objective facts and circumstances which are consistent with the shortterm effects of substance abuse or alcohol misuse. Examples of reasonable suspicion include, but are not limited to, the following: 
(1)  Physical signs and symptoms consistent with prohibited substance use or alcohol misuse. 
(2)  Evidence of the manufacture, distribution, dispensing, possession or use of controlled or prohibited substances, drugs or alcohol. 
(3)  Occurrence of a serious or potentially serious accident that may have been caused by prohibited substance abuse or alcohol misuse. 
(4)  Fights (assault or battery) and flagrant disregard or violation of established safety, security or other operating procedures. 
Reasonable suspicion referrals must be made by a supervisor who is trained to detect the signs and symptoms of drug and alcohol use and who reasonably concludes that an employee may be adversely affected or impaired in his work performance due to possible prohibited substance abuse and alcohol misuse. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 6.3, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-72. - Post-accident testing. 
(a)  All safety-sensitive and nonsafety-sensitive employees will be required to undergo urine and breath testing if they are involved in an accident with a county vehicle (on or off duty) that results in a fatality. This includes all surviving safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employees that are operating such vehicle or a passenger in such vehicle and any other safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employee whose performance could have contributed to the accident. A post-accident test will also be conducted if an accident results in injuries requiring immediate transportation to a medical treatment facility; or one (1) or more vehicles incurs disabling damage; or the employee receives a citation under state or local law for a moving violation arising from the accident. If no citation is given, the county system's safety-sensitive and nonsafety-sensitive employee may still be tested if such employee cannot be completely discounted as a contributing factor to the accident. 
(b)  Following an accident, the safety-sensitive and nonsafety-sensitive employee will be tested as soon as possible, but not to exceed eight (8) hours for alcohol testing and thirty-two (32) hours for drug testing. Any safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employee involved in an accident must refrain from alcohol use for eight (8) hours following the accident or until he/she undergoes a post-accident alcohol test. Any safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employee who leaves the scene of an accident without justifiable explanation prior to submission to drug and alcohol testing will be considered to have refused the test and his employment will be terminated. Employees tested under this section will include not only the operations personnel, but any other covered employee whose performance could have contributed to the accident. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 6.4, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-73. - Random testing. 
Employees in assigned positions will be subject to random, unannounced drug and alcohol tests. The selection of safety-sensitive and nonsafety-sensitive employees for random alcohol testing will be made using a scientifically valid method that ensures each covered employee will have an equal chance of being selected each time selections for random testing are made. The random tests will be unannounced and spread throughout the year. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 6.5, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-74. - Return-to-duty testing. 
All safety-sensitive and nonsafety-sensitive employees who previously tested positive on a drug or alcohol test must test negative for alcohol (below 0.02) and drugs and be evaluated and released to duty by the substance abuse professional before returning to work. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 6.6, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-75. - Followup testing. 
Safety-sensitive and nonsafety-sensitive employees will be required to undergo frequent, unannounced urine and breath testing following their return to duty. The followup testing will be performed for a period of one (1) to five (5) years with a minimum of six (6) tests to be performed the first year. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 6.7, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-76. - Employment assessment. 
Any safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employee who tests positive for the presence of illegal drugs or alcohol above the minimum thresholds set forth in 49 CFR 40, as amended, will be referred for evaluation by a substance abuse professional. A "substance abuse professional" is a licensed or certified physician, psychologist, social worker, employee assistance professional or addiction counselor with knowledge of and clinical experience in the diagnosis and treatment of alcohol-related disorders. The substance abuse professional will evaluate each employee to determine what assistance, if any, the employee needs in resolving problems associated with prohibited drug use or alcohol misuse. Assessment by a substance abuse professional or participation in the county's employee assistance program does not shield an employee from disciplinary action or guarantee employment or reinstatement with the county. If a safety-sensitive or nonsafety-sensitive employee is allowed to return to duty, he/she must properly follow the rehabilitation program prescribed by the substance abuse professional, he/she must have negative return-to-duty drug and alcohol tests and be subject to unannounced followup testing for a period of one (1) to five (5) years. The cost of any treatment or rehabilitation services will be paid directly by the employee or his insurance provider. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, § 7.0, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-77. - Disciplinary actions. 
(a)  Employees removed from their employment positions for violation of this division shall, for the first offense, utilize any accumulated sick, vacation or holiday leave. If there are no leave hours remaining, the employee will be placed on unpaid suspension. 
(b)  Refusal by the employee to submit to testing constitutes a violation of this division and shall result in termination of employment of such employee or other disciplinary action. 
(c)  Failure to successfully complete prescribed treatment will result in the employee's termination. 
(d)  A second positive test result shall require the employee's termination. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, §§ 8.1—8.4, 6-6-1996) 
Sec. 2-78. - Information disclosure. 
(a)  The county shall release information regarding a covered employee's record as directed by specific written consent from the employee authorizing release of the information to an identified person. 
(b)  A covered employee is entitled, upon written request, to obtain copies of any records pertaining to his use of prohibited substances, including any records pertaining to tests for such prohibited substances. 
(c)  The county may disclose information that is required to be maintained to the decision-maker in a lawsuit, grievance or other proceeding initiated by or on behalf of the employee tested for prohibited substances. 
(d)  When requested by the National Transportation Safety Board as part of an accident investigation, the county shall disclose information related to its administration of drug and alcohol tests following the accident investigation. 
(e)  Records shall be made available to subsequent employers upon receipt of written request from the covered employee. 
(f)  The county shall disclose data for its drug and alcohol testing program, and any other information pertaining to its antidrug program, when requested by the secretary of transportation or any department of transportation agency with regulatory authority over the county transit system. 
(Ord. No. O-1-96, §§ 9.1—9.6, 6-6-1996) 
Secs. 2-79—2-100. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - INDEMNIFICATION OF PERSONNEL 

Sec. 2-101. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Commission means the board of commissioners. 
Claim includes all claims presented against an employee prior to institution of a proceeding. 
Employee means any member of the board of commissioners, employees of the county and elected or appointed county officers and their appointees and employees, including appointed members of county boards, commissions, councils and authorities, past, present and future. The word "employee" does not include any member of the county board of education or any employee, officer or appointee of such board or the county school system. 
Proceeding includes any matter of a civil nature in or before any court or agency of this state, any other state or the United States. 
(Ord. No. O-3-97, § 1-A, 9-4-1997) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 2-102. - Defense of employees. 
Whenever any claim is made or proceeding is brought against an employee, either against him/her asserting personal liability for damages arising out of the performance of his duties or in any way connected with the performance of his duties, whether based on negligence, violation of contract rights or violation of civil, constitutional, common law or other statutory rights, whether federal, state or local, the county shall, upon the employee's written request, provide for the employee's defense unless otherwise limited by the terms of this division. The board of commissioners may decline defense of an employee if the employee fails to provide notice in writing of any claim or proceeding to the commission within thirty (30) days after the employee has received notice of a claim or within ten (10) days after the employee has been served with process in a proceeding initiated against the employee. 
(Ord. No. O-3-97, § 1-B, 9-4-1997) 
Sec. 2-103. - Grounds for refusal of defense. 
(a)  The county shall refuse to provide for the defense of a claim or proceeding brought against any employee if it determines that: 
(1)  The act or omission did not arise out of and in the course of his employment; 
(2)  The employee acted or failed to act because of actual or intentional misconduct, fraud, corruption or malice; 
(3)  Defense of the claim or proceeding by the county would create a conflict of interest between the county and the employee; 
(4)  The proceeding is a criminal prosecution; 
(5)  Provision of a defense against the claim or proceeding would not be in the best interest of the county; 
(6)  The employee acts or fails to act as a result of, or at a time when, his own self-indulgence substantially impaired his judgment, as, for example, an officer or employee who causes damage or injury while under the influence of drugs or alcohol while on the job; 
(7)  The employee acts or fails to act, except in emergencies or the existence of extenuating circumstances, directly contrary to the advice of the county attorney; 
(8)  The employee acts or fails to act in such manner as to constitute a criminal act, as, for example, misappropriation of property or funds; 
(9)  The employee acted or failed to act in a willful disregard of county policy or specific instructions of the employee's supervisor; or 
(10)  The employee fails to cooperate in the defense of the claim or proceeding. 
(b)  Nothing contained in this section shall be construed to prohibit the county from providing a defense against a claim or proceeding where there is a conflict of interest between one (1) employee, or group of employees, of the county and another employee, or group of employees, of the county. 
(c)  The determination required by subsection (a) of this section shall be made by the chairman of the board of commissioners. An appeal may be made by such employee to the commission in the event of a denial by the chairman. Such appeal must be submitted in writing within ten (10) days of the denial. 
(d)  Upon approval of the defense of a claim or proceeding against an employee, the chairman shall refer the matter to the county attorney for disposition; however, if two (2) or more employees are involved, and the interest of one (1) employee, or group of employees, conflicts with the interest of another employee, or group of employees, then, in such event, the commission shall specify which employee, or group of employees, shall be represented by the county attorney and shall authorize the other employee, or group of employees, to employ counsel at the expense of the county; provided, however, that the selection and compensation of such other counsel shall be subject to the prior approval of the commission. 
(Ord. No. O-3-97, § 1-C, 9-4-1997) 
Sec. 2-104. - Payment of judgments and settlement of claims. 
(a)  Where defense of a claim or proceeding against an employee is provided by this division, all final judgments awarded in courts of competent jurisdiction against such employee in proceedings to which this division applies or any amount payable under any settlement of such proceeding or of claims in accordance with this division may be paid, at the discretion of the board of commissioners, by the county, as provided in this section. All compromises of claims or proceedings governed by this division shall be submitted to the commission for prior approval. 
(b)  Notwithstanding subsection (a) of this section, payment of judgments and claims shall be limited to the following: 
(1)  No sum shall be paid where the employee's liability is based on a discretionary act, and the county and the employee reserve the right to asset all governmental and sovereign immunity in defense of such claims. Payment of judgments and claims pursuant to this section shall be made only where liability is based upon a ministerial act of the employee. It is the intent of this section to provide for the payment of claims and judgments only where the defense of sovereign and governmental immunity may not be asserted initially as a defense to the claim or proceeding. 
(2)  No sum shall be paid on behalf of an employee in any one (1) claim or proceeding in excess of fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00) for damages and not to exceed the total cost of one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) per occurrence, except that attorney's fees of plaintiff's attorneys shall be allowed in addition, if awarded. 
(3)  No sum shall be paid under the provisions of this division for punitive or exemplary damages awarded against any employee. 
(4)  No sum shall be paid under the provisions of this division unless the claimant unconditionally releases the employee and the county from any and all claims, causes of action or judgments arising out of the subject claim or proceeding. 
(5)  Excluded further from the operation of this division is any claim or proceeding for which insurance coverage is applicable. 
(Ord. No. O-3-97, § 1-D, 9-4-1997) 
Sec. 2-105. - Construction. 
(a)  Nothing contained in this division shall be deemed to constitute any waiver by the county of the governmental immunity afforded it under the constitution and laws of the state. Nothing contained in this division shall be interpreted in any way to reduce or eliminate the rights of any employee of the county against any other party. 
(Ord. No. O-3-97, § 1-E, 9-4-1997) 
Secs. 2-106—2-110. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - CODE ENFORCEMENT OFFICER 

Sec. 2-111. - Position created. 
There is hereby created the position of code enforcement officer. 
(Ord. No. 06-07-07(b), § 1, 6-7-2007) 
Sec. 2-112. - Duties and responsibilities. 
The primary duties and responsibilities of the code enforcement officer shall be as follows: 
(1)  To enforce all ordinances and codes heretofore or hereafter enacted by governing authority of the county, unless specific provisions in the ordinance or code expressly limit the enforcement powers of the code enforcement officer; 
(2)  To issue warnings, notices of ordinance or code violations, and summons and citations for court appearances for violations of ordinances and codes; 
(3)  To enter upon and inspect any building, land, structure or premises in the county for the purpose of ensuring compliance with all ordinances and codes; 
(4)  To investigate and collect evidence of ordinance and code violations; 
(5)  To respond to complaints of alleged ordinance and code violations; 
(6)  To appear and testify in court; 
(7)  To do any follow up work that may be necessary; 
(8)  To insure proper collection of fees, fines, and penalties; 
(9)  To coordinate enforcement efforts with other departments or divisions of the county as may be deemed necessary. 
(Ord. No. 06-07-07(b), § 2, 6-7-2007) 
Sec. 2-113. - Violations and penalties. 
Any person who shall violate any order of the code enforcement officer given in pursuance of and by the authority of this division, or who shall undertake actions intended to delay, frustrate, or hinder the code enforcement officer in the performance of duties described in this division, shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in § 1-19 of the county code of ordinances. 
(Ord. No. 06-07-07(b), § 3, 6-7-2007) 
Secs. 2-114—2-120. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - HARASSMENT AND SEXUAL HARASSMENT POLICY 

Sec. 2-121. - Definition of harassment. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Harassment is verbal or physical conduct that degrades or shows hostility or aversion toward an individual because of his or her race, color, religion, sex, national origin, age, disability or that of his or her relatives, friends, or associates and that: 
(1)  Has the purpose or effect of creating an intimidating, hostile, or offensive work environment; 
(2)  Has the purpose or effect of unreasonably interfering with an individual's work performance; 
(3)  Has the purpose or effect of unreasonably interfering with an individual's employment opportunities. 
Harassing conduct includes, but is not limited to, the following: 
(1)  Epithets, slurs, negative stereotyping, or threatening, intimidating, or hostile acts, that relate to race, color, religion, sex, national origin, age or disability; 
(2)  Written or graphic material that degrades or shows hostility or aversion toward an individual or group because of race, color, religion, sex, national origin, age, or disability and that is placed on walls, bulletin boards, or elsewhere on county premises or is circulated in the work place. 
(Res. R-16-01, § I, 5-3-2001) 
Sec. 2-122. - Harassment complaint procedures. 
Employees encountering harassment should tell the offending person that such conduct is inappropriate and offensive. The employee shall document all incidents of harassment in order to provide the fullest basis for investigation. In addition, the employee shall notify his or her supervisor of the harassment as soon as possible so that steps may be taken to protect the employee from further harassment and appropriate investigative and disciplinary measures may be initiated. If the employee works for the sheriff's department, tax commissioner, probate judge or superior court clerk, he or she shall report any alleged harassment to his or her immediate supervisor and/or the pertinent constitutional officer if possible and appropriate under the circumstances. Otherwise, such employee shall notify the county manager or the county's female designee of the alleged harassment. The county's female designee may be changed by resolution of the board of commissioners. 
(Res. R-16-01, § II, 5-3-2001) 
Sec. 2-123. - Definition of sexual harassment. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Inappropriate sexual advances, requests for sexual favors, and other physical, verbal or visual conduct based on sex constitutes sexual harassment when: 
(1)  Submission to such conduct is either explicitly or implicitly made a term or condition of an individual's employment; 
(2)  Submission to or rejection of such conduct by an individual is used as a basis for any employment decision affecting such individual; and/or 
(3)  Such conduct has the purpose and effect of unreasonably interfering with an individual's work performance or creating an intimidating, hostile or offensive working environment. 
Sexual harassment may include explicit sexual propositions, sexual innuendo, suggestive comments, sexually oriented "kidding" or "testing", practical jokes, jokes about gender or specific traits, foul or obscene language or gestures, displays of foul or obscene language or gestures, displays of foul or obscene printed or visual material, any physical contact, such as patting, pinching, or brushing against another's body. 
(Res. R-16-01, § III, 5-3-2001) 
Sec. 2-124. - Sexual harassment complaint procedures. 
(a)  All employees are responsible for helping to insure that harassment is avoided. If any employee feels that he or she has experienced or witnessed harassment, such employee shall notify either his or her immediate supervisor, the county manager, or the county's female designee. If the employee works for the sheriff's department, tax commissioner, probate judge or superior court clerk, he or she shall report any alleged harassment to his or her immediate supervisor and/or the pertinent constitutional officer if possible and appropriate under the circumstances. Otherwise, such employee shall notify the county manager or the county's female designee of the alleged harassment. Reports are to be made as soon as practicable, and preferably in writing. Oral reports, however, will be taken in the case of unusually sensitive circumstances. 
(b)  It shall be the county's policy to investigate all such complaints to the fullest extent practicable. The county will keep complaints and the terms of their resolution confidential. If an investigation confirms that sexual harassment has occurred, the county will take corrective action in accordance with the nature and extent of the offense. The county also prohibits retaliation against any employee bringing a claim of sexual harassment. 
(Res. R-16-01, § IV, 5-3-2001) 
Sec. 2-125. - Harassment and sexual harassment false accusation procedures. 
The county recognizes that false accusations of harassment and sexual harassment can have a serious effect on innocent men and women. Individuals falsely accusing another of harassment or sexual harassment will face corrective action in accordance with the nature and extent of his or her false accusation. 
(Res. R-16-01, § V, 5-3-2001) 
Sec. 2-126. - Sexual harassment and harassment employee inquiry procedures. 
The county encourages any employee to raise questions he or she may have regarding the harassment policy or sexual harassment with his or her immediate supervisor, constitutional officers, the county manager or the county's female designee. 
(Res. R-16-01, § VI, 5-3-2001) 
Sec. 2-127. - Dissemination of policy. 
The county deems harassment and sexual harassment to be a matter of concern. The county shall disseminate this harassment policy to all employees. Each employee will receive a copy of this policy and is instructed to read the policy. Each employee shall sign a statement one (1) week after delivery of the policy that the employee acknowledges receipt of this policy and has read this policy. 
(Res. R-16-01, § VII, 5-3-2001) 
Secs. 2-128—2-135. - Reserved.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-136. - Board of Commissioners meetings. 
The regular monthly workshop and regular monthly meeting of the Dade County Commission shall be held in the Dade County Administration Building, Trenton, Georgia, on the first Thursday of every month, beginning at 6:00 p.m. The regular monthly meeting shall immediately follow the conclusion of the monthly workshop. 
(Res. No. R-21-10, 9-2-2010)

DIVISION 2. - HOUSING AUTHORITY 

Sec. 2-156. - Created. 
Pursuant to the Housing Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 8-3-1 et seq., there is created in and for the county a housing authority. 
(Res. of 11-7-1985) 
Sec. 2-157. - Composition; appointment. 
The housing authority shall be composed of five (5) commissioners who shall be residents of the county appointed by resolution of the board of commissioners. If a commissioner at any time ceases to be a resident of the county, his term of office shall end. 
(Res. of 11-7-1985) 
Sec. 2-158. - Terms. 
The commissioners appointed to the housing authority shall serve for terms of five (5) years, provided the initial commissioners shall be appointed in such a fashion that such terms shall be staggered annually. If at the end of any term of office of any commissioner a successor thereto shall not have been elected, the commissioner whose term of office shall have expired shall continue to hold office until his successor shall be so elected. 
(Res. of 11-7-1985) 
Sec. 2-159. - Powers. 
The housing authority shall have the powers granted to it under state law to issue revenue bonds for the purpose of providing funds to finance housing in the county. 
(Res. of 11-7-1985) 
Sec. 2-160. - Compensation; expenses. 
No member of the housing authority shall receive any compensation for serving as a commissioner, but may be reimbursed for his actual expenses incurred in the performance of his duties. 
(Res. of 11-7-1985) 
Secs. 2-161—2-180. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - DEVELOPMENT AUTHORITY 

Sec. 2-181. - Created. 
Pursuant to the Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq., there is created in and for the county a development authority. 
(Res. of 6-11-1980) 
Sec. 2-182. - Composition; appointment. 
The development authority shall be composed of seven (7) directors who shall be taxpayers of the county and one (1) of whom is an officer or employee of the county appointed by resolution of the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 6-11-1980) 
Sec. 2-183. - Terms. 
The directors appointed to the development authority shall serve for terms of six (6) years, provided the initial directors shall be appointed in such a fashion that such terms shall be staggered. If at the end of any term of office of any director a successor thereto shall not have been elected, the director whose term of office shall have expired shall continue to hold office until his successor shall be so elected. 
(Res. of 6-11-1980) 
Sec. 2-184. - Powers. 
The development authority shall have the powers granted to it under state law to issue revenue bonds for the purpose of developing and promoting for the public good and general welfare trade, commerce, industry and employment opportunities in the county, thereby promoting the general welfare of the citizenry. 
(Res. of 6-11-1980) 
Secs. 2-185—2-205. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - AREA PLANNING COMMISSION 

Sec. 2-206. - Membership. 
The Coosa Valley Area Planning and Development Commission shall consist of two (2) members from each of the counties participating in the area planning commission. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 1) 
Sec. 2-207. - Appointment. 
Of the two (2) members of the area planning commission from each county, one (1) shall be appointed by the governing authority of the municipality wherein the county seat is located and the other shall be appointed by the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 1) 
Sec. 2-208. - Term of office. 
The term of office for all members of the area planning commission shall be five (5) years, except that the initial appointment by this county shall be for a term of three (3) years. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 2) 
Sec. 2-209. - Filling of vacancies. 
Any vacancy occurring in the membership of the area planning commission shall be filled for the unexpired term by the governing authority making the appointment which has become vacant. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 2) 
Sec. 2-210. - Removal. 
The appointing authority shall have the power to remove any member of the area planning commission it may appoint for cause, on written charges, after a public hearing. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 2) 
Sec. 2-211. - Compensation. 
All members of the area planning commission shall serve without compensation. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 2) 
Sec. 2-212. - Organization. 
The area planning commission shall adopt rules for the transaction of business and shall keep a record of its resolutions, transactions, findings and determinations, which record shall be a public record. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 3) 
Sec. 2-213. - Officers. 
The area planning commission shall elect a chairman and vice-chairman from among its appointive members. The term of the office of the chairman and vice-chairman shall be for one (1) year or until reelected or their successors are elected. The area planning commission shall appoint a secretary who may be an employee of the commission. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 3) 
Sec. 2-214. - Meetings. 
The area planning commission shall meet at least once each month at the call of the chairman and at such other times as the chairman or board of commissioners may determine. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 3) 
Sec. 2-215. - Employees and staff. 
The area planning commission may appoint such employees and staff as it may deem necessary for its work. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 3) 
Sec. 2-216. - Interagency cooperation; expenditures. 
In the performance of its duties, the area planning commission may cooperate with, contract with or accept funds from federal, state or local public or semipublic agencies or private individuals or corporations, may spend such funds and may carry out such cooperative undertakings and contracts. The commission may make expenditures for the purchase of required equipment and supplies. The expenditures of the commission, exclusive of gifts to the commission and contract receipts, shall be within the amounts appropriated for the purpose by the participating governing authorities. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 3) 
Sec. 2-217. - Powers; duties. 
It shall be the function and duty of the area planning commission to make such careful and comprehensive surveys and studies of existing conditions and probable future developments and to prepare such plans for physical, social and economic growth as will best promote the public health, safety, morals, convenience, prosperity or the general welfare as well as efficiency and economy in the development of the entire northwest Georgia area and each political subdivision therein. In general, the area planning commission shall have such powers, duties and responsibilities as set forth in this division. 
(Res. of 11-15-1960, § 4) 
Secs. 2-218—2-250. - Reserved.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 2-251—2-270. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PURCHASING 
Subdivision I. - In General 

Sec. 2-271. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
County agency means any department or division of the county government. 
IFB means an invitation for bid. 
LPA means a limited purchase allowance. 
PO means a purchase order. 
PR means a purchase requisition. 
Purchasing agent means the county manager or his designee, who is authorized and responsible for the procurement of supplies and services for county use. 
RFQ means a request for quotation. 
Vendor means any person or company that sells supplies and/or services. 
(Ord. No. O-11-12-99, § I(A), 2-3-2000) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 2-272. - Program objectives. 
(a)  Purchasing program objectives are essential to the implementation and administration of a meaningful, viable and successful purchasing program. Purchasing program objectives spell out in words what is expected of the purchasing program and of the individuals who administer and participate in the purchasing program. Purchasing program objectives also serve as a set of guidelines to be used by management, operation personnel and the purchasing agent in reaching responsible and intelligent decisions relative to the day-to-day administration of the purchasing program. Purchasing program objectives provide management with a set of general standards against which to gauge the effectiveness and success of the purchasing program. 
(b)  The primary objectives of the county purchasing program are to: 
(1)  Establish an ongoing centralized purchasing function capable of providing daily service and support on an organization-wide basis. 
(2)  Introduce a greater measure of responsibility and accountability over implementation of the annual budget, specifically as related to the procurement of commodities, contractual services and capital outlay items. 
(3)  Ensure realization of the principles of competitive purchasing and the best buy at the least cost. 
(4)  Assist management at all levels in reaching responsible cost-effective decisions in the procurement of quality supplies and services for county use. 
(5)  Formulate policies and procedures designed to systematize and enhance the efficiency of the county procurement process and ensure procurement in a timely and proper manner. 
(6)  Promote goodwill and clear communication in county-vendor relations and intraorganization relations relative to purchasing. 
(7)  Promote the realization of equal opportunity policies through procurement relations with vendors. 
(Ord. No. O-11-12-99, § I(B), 2-3-2000) 
Sec. 2-273. - Inventory. 
(a)  The county purchasing agent shall make an inventory of all county-owned equipment, furniture, fixtures and vehicles, describing each by model and serial number and setting out to which office such property is assigned. 
(b)  Upon the completion of such inventory as set forth in subsection (a) of this section, the county purchasing agent shall furnish a list of the property assigned to each office to the department head or office holder acknowledging such property is in fact located in that office; thereafter, each item of such property that is purchased for such office or department costing in excess of five hundred dollars ($500.00), or has a life expectancy of three (3) years or longer, shall, upon its delivery, be assigned to the department or office holder, and such item shall be added to the inventory of such department. 
(c)  The inventory of property assigned to each office shall be maintained as a permanent record in the office of the county manager. Upon reassignment of the use of such property between departments, a receipt for the property shall be taken from the department head receiving it, and the property shall be removed from the inventory list of the department from which it is removed and shall be added to the inventory list of the department to which it is assigned. 
(d)  Annually, the county purchasing agent shall inventory the property of each office and present the inventory to the department head of such office and shall file such annual inventory with the permanent record. 
(e)  Upon the retirement, resignation or discharge of any department head, an inventory shall be taken of each office and all property charged to that department shall be satisfactorily accounted for. 
(Ord. No. O-11-12-99, § I(C), 2-3-2000) 
Secs. 2-274—2-290. - Reserved. 
Subdivision II. - Administration 

Sec. 2-291. - In general. 
(a)  The authority and responsibility for maintaining a centralized purchasing program shall reside in the county manager as purchasing agent, or his designee, and his immediate staff. This places the responsibility on those who have the interest and skill to do the procedure work properly and whose primary concern is the performance of uniform policies covering county-vendor relationships as well as interdepartment relationships and permits adequate controls to be exercised over expenditures. 
(b)  The purpose of this subdivision is to establish a set of policies designed to guide the decision process as it relates to the procurement of supplies and services for use by the county. 
(Ord. No. O-11-12-99, § II(A), 2-3-2000) 
Sec. 2-292. - Centralized purchasing. 
It shall be the policy of the county to maintain a centralized purchasing process with the purchasing agent. It shall be the purchasing agent's responsibility to administer purchasing policies, institute reports necessary to permit analysis of purchasing performance, negotiate and approve term contracts in concert with county departments, consolidate purchases of like or common items, analyze prices paid for materials and equipment and generally define how to obtain savings and to coordinate purchasing procedures. 
(Ord. No. O-11-12-99, § II(B), 2-3-2000) 
Sec. 2-293. - Supply sources. 
The purchasing agent shall select supply sources in concert with the appropriate department. This shall be accomplished with a view toward creating good vendor relations and promoting the best interest of the county. The county recognizes that frankness and fair dealing comprise the cornerstones to strong and lasting relationships with suppliers.
