(6)  If the applicant is a limited liability company, the application shall be made jointly in the name of the limited liability company and its managers, and any member owning at least a twenty percent (20%) interest in the assets or revenues of the limited liability company. 
(7)  If the applicant is an entity other than a natural person, partnership, limited partnership, limited liability partnership, corporation or a limited liability company, the application shall be made jointly in the name of the entity, the natural person having chief executive officer authority over the business activities of the entity and any other person having at least a five percent (5%) interest in the assets or revenues of the entity. The application shall further disclose the type of entity making the application and every person having an ownership interest in the assets or revenues of the entity. 
(8)  Licenses issued to corporations, limited liability companies, general partnerships, limited partnerships, limited liability partnerships or other types of entities must be issued jointly to the entity, and all of the other persons required by this section to join in the application. 
(9)  No person shall be granted a license unless it shall appear to the satisfaction of the license review board that such person shall be of good moral character, or in the case of an entity which is not a natural person, that such entity has a good reputation. In no event shall a license be granted to any person who has been convicted or has pled guilty or entered a plea of nolo contendere to any charge involving a crime of moral turpitude, prostitution, masturbation for hire or any other sexual service crime within a period of ten (10) years immediately prior to the filing of such application. In the case of partnerships, corporations, limited partnerships, limited liability partnerships, limited liability companies or other business entities, an operator's license shall not be issued to the partnership, corporation, limited partnership, limited liability partnership, limited liability company or other entity if any partner, officer, director, shareholder, member or other person required to be listed on the application cannot meet the requirements set forth in this subsection. At the time an application is submitted for an operator's license, the applicant shall, by a duly sworn affidavit: 
a.  Certify that all of the requirements of this section have been met by the applicant and the other persons required to be listed on the application as specified in this subsection (9); and 
b.  Consent to a criminal background check and release the county, its commissioners, elected officials, officers, agents, employees and representatives from any liability resulting from any criminal background check performed on the applicant. 
After the license has been issued, should any person in whose name such license is issued be convicted of or plead guilty or nolo contendere to a charge involving a crime of moral turpitude, prostitution, masturbation for hire or any other sexual service crime, the operator's license shall be immediately revoked and canceled. 
(10)  No operator's license shall be issued to any person convicted of or pleading guilty or nolo contendere to any charge under any federal, state or local law constituting a felony, within ten (10) years prior to the date of the filing of the application for the operator's license. 
(11)  No operator's license shall be issued to any person who has had any license issued under the police powers of the county revoked within two (2) years prior to the filing of the application for an operator's license. 
(12)  The license review board may decline to issue an operator's license when any person having any ownership interest in or control over the land or building in which the establishment to be operated pursuant to the license will be located does not meet the same character requirements as set forth in this section for the licensee. 
(13)  If a person in whose name an operator's license is issued is not a resident of the county, such person must appoint and continuously maintain in the county a registered agent upon whom any process, notice or demand required or permitted by law or under this chapter may be served. The registered agent must be a resident of the county. If the licensee is not a natural person, the licensee will be required to appoint and maintain a registered agent in the county if it does not have an agent in the county upon whom process can legally be served on such entity under the laws of the state. The licensee shall file the name of such registered agent, along with such registered agent's written consent to serve as such agent, with the director of administrative services. 
(14)  An application for an operator's license may be denied where it appears to the license review board that the applicant does not have adequate financial strength or adequate financial participation in the proposed business to direct and manage its affairs, or where it appears that the applicant is intended or likely to be a surrogate for a person who would not otherwise qualify for an operator's license. 
(15)  At the time of filing the application for an operator's license and thereafter, the applicant must at all time have in his or her employ or under a binding contract, a person who holds a massage license issued by the state who has agreed to perform the massage services for the applicant if the operator's license is granted. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 3, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-4. - Establishment of license review board. 
A license review board is created to receive and consider applications for licenses to operate massage businesses and for all other purposes necessary to administer this chapter. The license review board created by this chapter shall be the same board as the alcoholic beverage control board previously established by §§ 6-31 et seq., of the county code of ordinances, and shall have the same composition, tenure, method of appointment, chairman, and clerk, as the alcoholic beverage control board, and shall be for all intents and purposes the same board, but with the additional powers, duties, and responsibilities as provided under this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 4, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-5. - Revocation, suspension of license. 
(a)  Any license granted under this chapter shall be subject to revocation or suspension for cause. Whenever, in the opinion of the license review board, there is cause to revoke or suspend an operator's or massage license, a written notice of intention to revoke or suspend such license shall notify the holder thereof not less than ten (10) days before a scheduled hearing with the license review board, at which time the holder of the license may make such showing as the licensee may deem proper. After a hearing, the license review board may revoke or suspend the license if, in its discretion, it is in the best interest of peace and good order of the county, or there has been any violation of the ordinances of the county or of the laws of the United States or the State of Georgia in the conduct of the massage business or on the massage business premises, or in the performing of massage services to members of the public. 
(b)  Cause for revocation or suspension of a license under this chapter shall include, but not be limited to, the following actions: 
(1)  Conviction of or a plea of guilty or nolo contendere to a charge of prostitution, masturbation for hire or any other sexual service crime involving the engaging in sexual activities for compensation or sexual misconduct of any kind by an employee of the massage business operated pursuant to such license, in the course of business. 
(2)  Providing false or forged information in the application to obtain a license under this chapter. 
(3)  Impersonating a license holder. 
(4)  Using or attempting to use a license that has expired or been revoked. 
(5)  Failure to maintain in employ or under a binding contract at least one (1) person who holds a massage therapy license issued by the state. 
(6)  Violation of any provision of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 5, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-6. - Appeal procedures. 
In all instances in which an application for a license is denied, or a license is revoked, suspended, or not renewed, under the terms of this chapter, the applicant or licensee may appeal the decision to the county board of commissioners by filing with the county clerk a request for such appeal within ten (10) days of the date that notice was mailed to the applicant or licensee of the license review board's decision. The request for such appeal must be dated, in writing, and must state the grounds and reasons for the appeal. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 6, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-7. - Automatic license forfeiture of nonuse. 
Any licensee holding an operator's license under this chapter, who shall, for a period of three (3) consecutive months, cease to operate the massage business as authorized in the operator's license, shall automatically forfeit the license without the necessity of any further action. If the massage business operation is interrupted as a result of damage to the premises where the massage business is located which makes it impractical to operate the massage business, and if repairs of such damage are commenced within such three-month period and diligently pursued to completion, or as a result of the premises being remodeled, then this section shall not apply to such cessation of operation. If a license is issued for the operation of a massage business in a building which has not yet been completed, the license will not be forfeited unless the licensee fails to begin operations of the massage business within a period of one hundred eighty (180) days from the date of issuance of the license. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 7, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-8. - Initial application; expiration; renewal of license. 
(a)  Each initial application for an operator's license shall make written application to the license review board. Such application shall be on a form approved by the clerk or the deputy clerk. 
(b)  The license application shall be filed with the clerk with a fee as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the county clerk for the processing and investigation of the application. Such fee is not refundable; but the application fee shall be credited to the fee amount due for the initial license, if granted. 
(c)  Each license granted under this chapter shall expire on December 31 of the calendar year in which the license was issued, and shall be renewable at the option of the license review board. A licensee who desires to renew his license shall file a written application on the form provided for license renewal on or before November 1 of each year. If a renewal application is received after November 1, the county cannot assure the applicant that a renewal license will be considered by January 1 of the following calendar year, and the licensee will have to cease operations from such January 1 until the renewal license is issued. If a license renewal application is received after the December 31 expiration date, such application shall be treated as an application for a new license and the applicant shall be required to comply with all rules, regulations and fees for the granting of licenses as if no previous license had been issued. 
(d)  Any person applying for renewal of a license must pay the license fees as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the county clerk for the processing and investigation of the license renewal application. Failure to pay such fees at that time shall result in the application for renewal being treated as not filed or as being withdrawn. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 8, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-9. - Location of business; hours of operation; separate application and operator's license for each business location. 
(a)  Prohibited location. No operator's license shall be granted under this chapter to a business premises located within the following areas of the county: 
(1)  Within a measured five hundred (500) feet of any church building. The word building , as used in this section, shall mean a structure used at the time of filing of the application for a license under this chapter for the purposes of church. For the purpose of this chapter, a church shall mean an organization for the purpose of preaching the gospel and other related religious activities located within a permanent structure either owned or leased by such organization, and shall consist of at least ten (10) adult members on the official rolls that meet on a regularly scheduled basis not less than one (1) time per week at such location. 
(2)  Within five hundred (500) feet measured in a straight line from the nearest property line of any school or schoolhouse to the nearest corner of the premises on which the massage business is to be operated. 
(3)  In any existing building or establishment having a history or reputation, within the six (6) months preceding the filing of the application, for prostitution or other sex offenses; fighting, shooting, stabbing, or other violence; gambling; illegal dealing in alcoholic beverages or drugs; or other violations of the law. 
(b)  All massage businesses licensed under this chapter shall remain closed between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 8:00 a.m. 
(c)  Each operator's license under this chapter shall be limited to the operation of a massage business at a specific premises. A separate application must be made and separate operator's licenses must be obtained for each location at which a massage business is conducted. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 9, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-10. - Display of license. 
(a)  An operator's license shall, at all times, be kept plainly exposed to public view at the premises for which the license was granted. 
(b)  A massage license shall, at all times, be kept plainly exposed to public view at the place where the holder of the massage license is performing massage services. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 10, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-11. - Report of licensed employees. 
Within ten (10) days after a written request of the license review board, a holder of an operator's license under this chapter shall provide a list of the names and addresses of those individuals holding a massage therapy license from the state and who are in the licensee's employ or under a binding contract with the licensee issued by the state. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 11, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-12. - Enforcement of other laws not limited; severability; effective date. 
(a)  This chapter shall not limit the authority of any state, local agency, or county department to enforce any other laws, rules, regulations, or ordinances. 
(b)  In the event any section, subsection, sentence, clause, or phrase of this chapter is declared or adjudged to be unconstitutional, or otherwise contrary to law, such adjudication shall in no manner affect any other section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase, and shall remain in full force and effect as if the section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase so declared or adjudged invalid or unconstitutional was not originally a part hereof. 
(c)  Any person operating a massage business upon the effective date of this chapter shall have ninety (90) days from such effective date to comply with this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 12, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-13. - Transferability. 
No license under this chapter shall be transferable. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 13, 10-30-2007) 
Sec. 33-14. - Violation; penalties. 
(a)  Any violation of the provisions of this chapter shall constitute a misdemeanor and shall be punishable by penalties and costs as set forth in § 1-19 of the county code of ordinances. In the event any provision of this chapter has been violated or is being violated, in addition to other remedies, the county may institute an injunction, mandamus, or other appropriate action or proceeding to correct or stop such violation. 
(b)  In addition to the penalties set forth in subsection (a) of this section, the license review board may revoke or suspend a license for violation of this chapter as set forth in § 33-4, which shall be a distinct and separate penalty. Any violation of this chapter, or any failure to comply with the requirements of this chapter, shall be grounds for immediate suspension or revocation of any and all licenses held by the licensee regardless of the number of licenses or locations involved, and regardless of whether or not the licensee knew of or contributed to such violation. It is the intent of this subsection, without limiting the generality thereof, to grant to the license review board the right to suspend or revoke any and all licenses held by a licensee when any violation of this chapter occurs at any place of business operated by the licensee pursuant to a license. 
(Ord. No. 10-30-07(b), § 14, 10-30-2007) 
Chapter 34 - OFFENSES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Traffic and vehicles, ch. 54. 
State Law reference— Limitation on home rule powers of municipal corporations with respect to duplication of state criminal offenses, O.C.G.A. § 36-35-6(a)(2); criminal code of Georgia, O.C.G.A. § 16-1-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - SMOKING 

Sec. 34-1. - Smoking in county-owned facilities. 
It is resolved by the board of commissioners that no smoking will be permitted in the county justice building, county courthouse and county health department building. 
(Res. of 5-4-1993) 
Sec. 34-2. - Smoking in county parks. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Department means the county parks and recreation department, a department under the jurisdiction of the board of commissioners. 
Parks means all parks and all facilities located thereon, owned and/or controlled by the county and operated under the jurisdiction of the county parks and recreation department. 
Person means any individual, citizen, group, association, firm, corporation or other legal entity who is authorized to use and enjoy the county's parks and any structure or facility located therein. 
(b)  Prohibited acts. It shall be unlawful for any person to smoke or to otherwise use tobacco products in all parks, except in those areas specifically designated and marked as smoking areas by the county parks and recreation department. 
(c)  Violation; penalties. In addition to penalties which may be imposed under state law for the violation of O.C.G.A. § 16-12-2, any violation of the provisions of this section shall constitute a misdemeanor and shall be punishable by penalties and costs as set forth in § 1-19 of the county code of ordinances. 
(d)  Enforcement of other laws not limited; severability; effective date. 
(1)  This section shall not limit the authority of any state, county, or other governmental agency to enforce any other applicable laws, rules, regulations, or ordinances. 
(2)  In the event any section, subsection, sentence, clause, or phrase of this section is declared or adjudged to be unconstitutional, or otherwise contrary to law, such adjudication shall in no manner affect any other section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase, and shall remain in full force and effect as if the section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase so declared or adjudged invalid or unconstitutional was not originally a part hereof. 
(3)  This section shall become effective immediately upon its adoption, and all ordinances in conflict with this section are repealed to the extent of the conflict. 
(Ord. No. 12-03-09, §§ 1—4, 12-3-2009) 
Secs. 34-3—34-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - WATER CONSERVATION 

Sec. 34-21. - Restriction on outdoor water of landscape. 
Outdoor watering for purposes of planting, growing, managing, or maintaining ground cover, trees, shrubs, or other plants in the unincorporated area may occur only between the hours of 4:00 p.m. and 10:00 a.m.; provided, however, that this limitation shall not create any limitation upon the following outdoor water uses: 
(1)  Commercial raising, harvesting, or storing of crops; feeding, breeding, or managing livestock or poultry; the commercial production or storing of feed for use in the production of livestock, including, but not limited to, cattle, calves, swine, hogs, goats, sheep, and rabbits, or for use in the production of poultry, including, but not limited to, chickens, hens, ratites, and turkeys; producing plants, trees, fowl, or animals; or the commercial production of aqua-cultural, horticultural, dairy, livestock, poultry; eggs, and apiarian products or as otherwise defined in O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3; 
(2)  Capture and reuse of cooling system condensate or storm water in compliance with applicable ordinances and state guideline; 
(3)  Reuse of gray water in compliance with O.C.G.A. § 31-3-5.2 and applicable local board of health regulations; 
(4)  Use of reclaimed waste water by a designated user from a system permitted by the Environmental Protection Division of the Georgia Department of Natural Resources to provide reclaimed waste water; 
(5)  Watering personal food gardens; 
(6)  Watering new and replanted plant, seed, or turf in landscapes, golf courses, or sports turf fields during installation and for a period of thirty (30) days immediately following the date of installation; 
(7)  Drip irrigation or irrigation using soaker hoses; 
(8)  Hand watering with a hose with automatic cutoff or handheld container; 
(9)  Use of water withdrawn from private water wells or surface water by an owner or operator of property if such well or surface water is on the property; 
(10)  Watering horticultural crops held for sale, resale, or installation; 
(11)  Watering athletic fields, golf courses, or public turf grass recreational areas; 
(12)  Installation, maintenance, or calibration of irrigation systems; or 
(13)  Hydroseeding. 
(Ord. No. 12-02-10, § 1, 12-2-2010) 
Sec. 34-22. - Enforcement. 
(a)  No person shall use or allow the use of water in violation of the restrictions on outdoor water use contained in this article. 
(b)  The Dade County Enforcement Officer and the Dade County Sheriff's Department shall be the enforcement authorities for this article. The Dade County Chairperson/County Executive may also authorize other departments as may be deemed necessary to support enforcement. 
(c)  Criminal and alternative penalties. Any violation of this article may also be enforced by a citation or accusation returnable to the Magistrate Court or by any other legal means as set forth in this Code. 
(Ord. No. 12-02-10, § 2, 12-2-2010) 
Secs. 34-23—34-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - CONTROLLED SUBSTANCES 

Sec. 34-41. - Sale or distribution of methadone. 
(a)  Definition. For the purpose of this section the following definition shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning. 
Person. Any individual, partnership, firm, association, joint venture, corporation, trust, estate, commission, board, institution, or any other legal entity, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. 
(b)  Prohibited acts. It shall be unlawful for any person to establish, own or operate a business having as its purpose the sale or distribution of the controlled substance within the unincorporated areas of the county without complying with federal and state laws and regulations for establishing, owning or operating such business. 
(c)  Penalty. Any violation of the provisions of this section shall be punishable by those penalties set forth in the federal or state laws or regulations violated, except that no penalties shall be in excess of or more severe than those set forth in § 1-19 of this Code. In addition to other remedies, the county may institute an action for an injunction, mandamus, or other appropriate action or proceeding to correct or stop such violation. 
(Ord. No. 04-07-11(a), §§ 1—3, 4-7-2011; Ord. No. 08-04-11, §§ 2, 3, 8-4-2011) 
Secs. 34-42—34-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - SAFETY REGULATIONS AND OTHER REQUIRMENTS FOR USE OF COUNTY PARKS 

Sec. 34-61. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Department means the county parks and recreation department, a department under the jurisdiction of the board of commissioners. 
Parks means all parks and all facilities located thereon, owned and/or controlled by the county and operated under the jurisdiction of the county parks and recreation department. 
Person means any individual, citizen, group, association, firm, corporation or other legal entity who is authorized to use and enjoy the county's parks and any structure or facility located therein. 
( Ord. No. 12-03-2015 , § 1, 12-3-2015) 
Sec. 34-62. - Prohibited acts. 
(a)  Pet leash required . No person who shall have in his or her possession or be responsible for any dog or other canine animal, whether or not the person be the owner of that animal, allow the same to run at large in any county parks, except as may otherwise be provided by law and this Code section. The health regulations and all other provisions appertaining to the control of domestic animals, including dogs, shall remain in full force and effect in county parks. It shall be the responsibility of any person bringing a dog into a county park to clean up any matter excreted by the dog. Nothing in this action shall amend or otherwise affect the penalties for violation of any law, ordinance, or regulation dealing with control of domestic animals which violation shall have occurred in areas other than within designated county parks. 
(b)  Conducting commercial activity. Except with written permission of the county, and only at the locations and times authorized by the county, no person may place or display any sign or advertisement in the parks, sell or offer for sale any merchandise or concessions, or engage in any other commercial activity in a county park. This provision shall not apply to county sponsored or authorized programs, festivals, or other events occurring in the parks. 
(c)  Participating in dangerous or destructive activities. No person shall ride a bicycle, skateboard, or other non-motorized vehicle in or on any park, except upon such trails or paths specifically designated for bicycling or other uses. No person shall play, practice, or otherwise participate in any game, sport, or other activity that is destructive to the lawn, plants, walls, road, or other infrastructure of a park, or to the health and safety of others reasonably using the park, except at or upon places designated for that game, sport or recreational activity. By way of example, these activities shall include but not be limited to skateboarding, treasure hunting, or golf. This section does not prohibit persons with disabilities from using a wheelchair as an auxiliary aid on county-owned or county-operated trails and paths. 
(d)  Entering closed ball fields. The county may close to the public particular ball-fields or other areas of county parks for maintenance purposes. Such closings shall be posted, and it shall be unlawful for any persons to enter a closed field or area until the ballpark or other area has been reopened. 
(e)  Littering. It shall be unlawful for any person to throw, dump, or deposit litter on the grounds, streets, sidewalks, creeks, or other body of water in any county parks. Where public receptacles are not provided, all such litter shall be carried away from the county park by the person responsible for its presence and shall be properly disposed of elsewhere. For purposes of this section, litter shall mean garbage, refuse, paper, rubbish, debris, trash, and all other waste material, whether natural or artificial. 
( Ord. No. 12-03-2015 , § 1, 12-3-2015) 
Sec. 34-63. - Violation; penalties. 
Any violation of the provisions of this article shall constitute a misdemeanor and shall be punishable by penalties and costs as set forth in section 1-19 of the Code of Ordinances of Dade County, Georgia. 
( Ord. No. 12-03-2015 , § 1, 12-3-2015) 
Chapter 35 - PARADES AND PUBLIC EVENTS 
ARTICLE I. - PARADES AND SPECIAL EVENTS 

Sec. 35-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Parade or special event: Any organized for-profit or nonprofit activity having as its purpose entertainment, recreation, fund raising, and/or education which takes place on state or county roads or rights of way in the unincorporated areas of Dade County, Georgia, and which requires or requests the temporary closing of state or county roads or rights of way. By way of example, special events include, but are not limited to, walks, races, parades, marches, processions, rallies, assemblies, festivals, concerts, holiday celebrations, bicycle runs, and block parties. 
Producer. Any person, group of persons, organization, association, club, or other entity responsible for planning, producing and conducting an event. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 1, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-2. - Permits required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, group, organization, association, club or other entity to conduct or cause to be conducted any parade or special event in unincorporated Dade County without having obtained a valid permit for such event. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 2, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-3. - Application; fee. 
(a)  A producer of a special event shall make application of a permit for such event at the office of the county executive on a form prescribed by the county executive. Application forms may be obtained from the office of the county executive. 
(b)  An application for a special event shall be filed with the county executive at least sixty (60) days prior to the date that event is scheduled to occur. However, no application shall be accepted earlier than one (1) year prior to the date of the event. 
(c)  A nonrefundable application fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) shall be paid at the time the application for a permit is filed. Such fee shall be payable to Dade County by cash, money order, or cashier's check. 
(d)  Events that are to occur along a route, including but not limited to, races, walks, runs, parades, marches, or processions, shall submit a map with the application for the permit, showing the exact route of the course for the event. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 3, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-4. - Administrative review. 
The county executive shall cause the application to be circulated to each government department and/or other agency whose services the county executive determines would be affected by the nature and activities of the proposed event. Each such department or agency shall review the application and note the services which it will be required to perform, the number of personnel to perform such services, the length of time to perform such services, the cost to perform such services, and any other information which would assist the county executive in facilitating the event and services required. For parades and special events, the county executive also shall cause the application to be forwarded to the district engineer of the Georgia department of transportation for review. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 4, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-5. - Special conditions on permit. 
Each county department reviewing an application may recommend in writing certain conditions or restrictions as deemed necessary to facilitate the event, to comply with other laws or regulations, and/or to ensure the safety, health and welfare of the community. In reviewing the recommendations of the department, the county executive may impose such conditions or restrictions as a part of the permit, and such special conditions so imposed shall be construed to have the full force and effect of law as a provision of this article. A violation of such conditions or restrictions shall be deemed a violation of this article. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 5, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-6. - Final approval of permit. 
The county executive is authorized to approve and issue a permit for a parade and special event after considering all comments and conditions of the reviewing departments and agencies as well as other information pertaining to the proposed events described on the application, and after the payment of all applicable fees and costs, and receiving the approval of the Georgia department of transportation when applicable. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 6, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-7. - Emergency issuance of permit. 
In extraordinary circumstances, the county executive shall be authorized to waive or otherwise expedite any or all of the review process and to issue a special event permit upon payment by the producer of all applicable fees and costs for such event. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 7, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-8. - Permit fees. 
(a)  The fee for a permit to conduct a special event shall be based on all services to be provided by the county for such event and shall be equal to the estimated actual cost to the county to provide such services. The initial permit fee shall be the aggregate of the estimated costs of such services calculated by each county department or agency The county executive may require a security bond or a cash deposit be provided by a producer, if it is determined that a security bond or deposit is necessary to provide for unanticipated expenses in connection with the event. 
(b)  The initial permit fee must be paid in full prior to the issuance of a permit and no later than seventy-two (72) hours prior to the date of the event. 
(c)  The fees required in this section shall be in addition to any other fees which may be required by any other ordinances or regulations that might be applicable. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 8, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-9. - Liability. 
The producer of any special event shall indemnify and hold harmless the government of Dade County, Georgia, its officers, department, constitutional officers, employees and agents from liability of damages arising from any acts or omissions emanating from a special event. Proof of such indemnification and waiver shall be filed with, and made a part of, the application form. The producer shall be responsible for providing liability insurance that may be necessary for any special event. The amount of liability insurance shall be based on the size of the event and shall designate the county as an additional insured. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 9, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-10. - Transferability and duration of permit. 
No permit under this article shall be transferable. No permit issued under this article shall be valid prior to or past the date of the special event for which it is issued. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 10, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-11. - Violation; penalties. 
Any violation of the provisions of this article shall constitute a misdemeanor and shall be punishable by penalties and costs as set forth in § 1-19 of the county code of ordinances. In the event any provision of the article has been violated or is being violated, in addition to other remedies, the county may institute an injunction, mandamus, or other appropriate action or proceeding to correct or stop such violation. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 11, 11-5-2009) 
Sec. 35-12. - Enforcement of other laws not limited; severability; effective date. 
(a)  This article shall not limit the authority of any state, county, or other governmental agency to enforce any other applicable laws, rules, regulations, or ordinances. 
(b)  In the event any section, subsection, sentence, clause, or phrase of this article is declared or adjudged to be unconstitutional, or otherwise contrary to law, such adjudication shall in no manner affect any other section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase, and shall remain in full force and effect as if the section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase so declared or adjudged invalid or unconstitutional was not originally a part hereof. 
(c)  This article shall become effective immediately upon its adoption, and all ordinances in conflict with this article are repealed to the extent of the conflict. 
(Ord. No. 11-05-09, § 12, 11-5-2009) 
Chapter 38 - ROADS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Any resolution or ordinance dedicating, naming, establishing, locating, relocating, opening, widening, paving, etc., any street or public way in the county saved from repeal, § 1-13(6); any resolution or ordinance providing for local improvements and assessing taxes for such local improvements saved from repeal, § 1-13(9); any resolution or ordinance establishing or prescribing street grades in the county saved from repeal, § 1-13(15); buildings and building regulations, ch. 18; flood control, ch. 26. 
State Law reference— State, county and municipal road systems, O.C.G.A. § 32-4-1 et seq.; power to construct and maintain roads, including curbs, sidewalks, street lights and devices to control the flow of traffic, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(4). 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 38-1—38-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ACCEPTANCE OF ROADS 

Sec. 38-31. - Subdivision development roads and rights-of-way. 
Subdivision development roads and rights-of-way proposals shall meet the following requirements: 
(1)  Proposals must be platted with base flood elevation data certified by a licensed surveyor. 
(2)  The development must have a minimum six-inch water main available for all lots if public water is available. Fire hydrants must be installed within one thousand (1,000) feet of any planned development. 
(3)  Drainage slopes must include adequate structures of concrete or metal culverts and drainage ditches which are a minimum of fifteen (15) inches deep. 
(4)  Access of a minimum of three (3) lots or five (5) mobile home lots for every one-third (⅓) of a mile. 
(5)  The development must have a dedicated sixty-foot right-of-way, thirty (30) feet each side of a road centerline; minimum twenty-four-foot roadbed with a five-foot shoulder on each side and thirteen (13) feet on each side available to ensure proper space for slopes, fills, drainage and utilities, for maintenance. 
(6)  Curbs and guttering are required if the development is designed with a fifty-foot right-of-way. The roadbed must be twenty-eight (28) feet, including curb and guttering, with eleven (11) feet each side available for utilities, slopes and shoulders, for maintenance. 
(7)  Eight (8) inches of compacted base which shall consist of six (6) inches of chert and two (2) inches of stone. 
(8)  The roadbed shall be graded smooth with minimum cuts or outcroppings. 
(9)  If the grade is less than six percent (6%), the roadbed shall be made of asphalt with two-inch E-mix. If the grade is higher than six percent (6%), a nonskid mix must be approved by the county road superintendent. 
(10)  Entry to a public road should be at a ninety-degree angle, where possible; however, the angle shall not exceed sixty (60) degrees. A landing for sixty (60) feet is required at no more than a two percent (2%) grade. 
(11)  A minimum of three (3) inspections must be completed by the county road superintendent at stages of development critical to excellent road construction. Final inspection will be after twelve (12) months. 
(Res. No. R 1-95, § I, 1-5-1995) 
Sec. 38-32. - Existing county road extensions (dead-end roads). 
Existing county road extensions (dead-end roads) shall have the following requirements: 
(1)  No utility relocations by the county. 
(2)  A minimum of a sixty-foot clear right-of-way deeded to the county, fee simple, after the twelve-month final inspection, and subsequent approval. 
(3)  The surface of the roadbed must conform to or exceed existing roadbed specifications as follows: 
a.  Six (6) inches of chert plus two (2) inches of stone or six (6) inches of compacted aggregate base. 
b.  Triple surface treatment according to county specifications. 
c.  The county road superintendent shall inspect the roadbed a minimum of two (2) times during construction. 
d.  The cul-de-sac shall be completed using roadbed and surface requirements as required by county specifications and shall have a minimum radius of fifty (50) feet. Additionally, the minimum radius of the right-of-way for the cul-de-sac shall be sixty-three (63) feet. 
(Res. No. R 1-95, § II, 1-5-1995; Res. No. R-20-07, 8-2-2007) 
Sec. 38-33. - Existing road extensions to another county road. 
Existing road extensions to another county road shall have the following requirements: 
(1)  The same requirements as set forth in section 38-32 but also must conform to the roadbed that has the higher specifications in place. 
(2)  If asphalt (E-mix) is required, the inspection must be performed a minimum of three (3) times during construction by the county road superintendent. 
(3)  A minimum of five (5) homes or eight (8) mobile homes must be in place for a minimum of five (5) years at the time of petition for acceptance. 
(Res. No. R 1-95, § III, 1-5-1995) 
Sec. 38-34. - State graded roads. 
State graded roads are required to have eighty-foot rights-of-way. The roadbed will conform to the twenty-four-foot requirement with five-foot shoulders on each side. 
(Res. No. R 1-95, § IV, 1-5-1995) 
Sec. 38-35. - Generally. 
(a)  The final inspection of any petitioned road must be completed by the county road superintendent a minimum of twelve (12) months after the last construction inspection. Drainage problems and poor quality construction will be considered prior to recommendation for county acceptance. 
(b)  Petitioners are not allowed to promise that the county will accept the road. If such promise is made, the petitioner must pay damages to the purchaser in such amounts prescribed by statute. 
(c)  The county will not accept any road that has a grade greater than ten percent (10%). 
(d)  Crossfalls must be a minimum of one-eighth (1/8) inch per foot on all finished surfaces. Super-elevated sections must be determined by the county road superintendent. 
(e)  The county may not desire to accrue a new road; therefore, even when the minimum standards have been met, the county may exercise its right not to accept a road into the system. 
(f)  Unless the county specifically desires to obtain a road, all efforts to obtain rights-of-way will be the responsibility of the party desiring to turn the road over to the county. 
(g)  When the county manager determines that a road qualifies for acceptance by the county, he/she will bring the matter before the board of commissioners. If the board of commissioners agrees that the road should be accepted, it will do so contingent on delivery of completed right-of-way deeds, within sixty (60) days. 
(h)  Alterations in the roadbed on existing roads must be presented to the county road superintendent and the county manager. If the determination is made to alter the roadbed for good reason, the petitioner must present a deed as required within sixty (60) calendar days after the board of commissioners has agreed to make such alterations. 
(Res. No. R 1-95, § V, 1-5-1995) 
Secs. 38-36—38-65. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - ROAD ADDRESSING 

Sec. 38-66. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Address program administrator means the official of the county charged with the administration of this article, including his authorized representative. The address program administrator shall be the 911 administrator of the county. 
Building means a structure for residential or business use, having a roof supported by columns or walls for the shelter of persons. When separated by division walls from the ground up, without openings, each such enclosure may be deemed a separate building. 
Concurrence means the board of commissioners shall have the right to disapprove any action of the address program administrator by a majority vote. If the board of commissioners shall fail to act within two (2) regular meetings after the action of the address program administrator, the board of commissioners shall be deemed to have concurred with such action of the address program administrator. 
Driveway means any private way, beginning at the property line of a lot abutting a public road, private road, easement or private right-of-way, giving access from the public road, private road, easement or private right-of-way, and leading to a building, lot or physical location. 
Private road means any one-way or two-way road for ingress and/or egress, not for use by the general public, that serves two (2) or more properties. 
Public road means any road, street, highway, thoroughfare or other way of passage that has been irrevocably dedicated to the public, or in which the public has acquired rights by prescription, without regard to whether such road is open for travel. 
Road address means the combination of numbers and road names assigned under the terms of this article which identifies a particular building, lot or other physical location. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 3, 12-7-1995) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 38-67. - Administration and application. 
The address program administrator, with the concurrence of the board of commissioners, will be responsible for the interpretation and administration of this article, including: 
(1)  Assigning all numbers for properties and buildings. 
(2)  Compiling a database of addresses of each property and building. 
(3)  Recommending change of existing addresses, when necessary, to facilitate sequential house numbers. 
(4)  Designating individual unit addresses within multiple housing units in conformity with this article. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 4, 12-7-1995) 
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2. 
Sec. 38-68. - Display of road address numbers. 
(a)  Every owner of improved property shall purchase and display official address numbers so that they are clearly visible from the street or road on which the property fronts. The following criteria shall be used to properly display such address number: 
(1)  Address numbers must be a minimum of three (3) inches in height for residential uses so as to be seen easily from the road. 
(2)  Numbers for multiple dwelling units and nonresidential buildings shall be at least six (6) inches in height and shall be placed on the front of the building facing the road or on the end of the building nearest the road. Individual units shall be required to display a unit number which shall be at least three (3) inches in height on the front door or immediately adjacent to the door. 
(3)  Address numbers must be set on a background of a contrasting color. 
(4)  On a corner lot, the house number should face the street named in the address. 
(5)  If a building is more than seventy-five (75) feet from any road, the address number shall be displayed on a sign attached to a fence gate, lawn stake, mailbox, etc., adjacent to and clearly visible from the road right-of-way. 
(6)  Address numbers shall be plain block numeric numbers and not in alpha or cursive style print. 
(b)  The address program administrator, with the concurrence of the board of commissioners, will have the right to authorize and approve alternate methods of displaying numbers which meet the intent of this article, when strict adherence to this article cannot be met. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 5, 12-7-1995) 
Sec. 38-69. - Types of numbers. 
The following types of numbers are to be used under this article: 
(1)  A primary number is to be assigned to each street frontage of each parcel of land, whether or not the parcel is occupied. The primary number is required to be posted only if the parcel is occupied by a dwelling unit, structure or active use and the owner, occupant or person in charge is notified as set forth in section 38-68. Other primary numbers are reserved for future development of the numbered parcels and will be assigned at the time of development. 
(2)  Secondary numbers may be used when a number of units, structures and uses coexist on the same parcel of land. Examples of parcels requiring secondary numbers include apartment projects, mobile home parks, office parks, planned unit developments, recreational vehicle parks, recreational areas, shopping centers and other uses where the use of secondary numbers would clarify the location of a unit or use for public safety purposes. To provide secondary numbers, the address program administrator shall work with the owner, manager or person in charge of the project to determine a logical numbering system under the following guidelines: 
a.  A building on a single parcel with more than one (1) and less than five (5) units may be given either letter (preferred) or number designations as requested by the owner of the property. 
b.  A single building on a single parcel of land with five (5) or more units may be given numerical designations such as suite number, apartment number or similar designations, if so desired. 
c.  Multiple buildings on the same parcel of land may be given secondary numbers consisting of number designation if the buildings are accessed from a main entrance to the project. The number designations should increase in a clockwise direction from the main entrance. 
d.  Mobile home parks, recreational vehicle parks and similar uses shall be given letter designations for lots or section and number designations for individual lots or sites. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 6, 12-7-1995) 
Sec. 38-70. - Exempt structures. 
The intent of this section is to exclude from this article those structures that do not present a significant danger to human life if destroyed by fire or other events. The following structures shall be excluded from the provisions of this article: 
(1)  Agricultural buildings not requiring a separate mailing address such as a barn, poultry house, outbuildings or equipment storage buildings. Buildings used as a dwelling unit, office or nominal work station of an employee shall not be exempt. 
(2)  Storage and accessory buildings for the use of the occupant of another building on the property. Buildings used as dwelling units, offices or the nominal work station of an employee, or requiring a separate mailing address, shall not be exempt. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 7, 12-7-1995) 
Sec. 38-71. - Existing road names. 
The names of roads listed on the official county road map sheet as developed by 911 that are located within the unincorporated areas of the county, whether public or private, shall not be changed by any methods except those set forth in this article. A copy of this article, and a list of road names, shall be forwarded to the department of transportation. The official county 911 road registry shall cross reference the old road names. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 8, 12-7-1995) 
Sec. 38-72. - New road names. 
(a)  No new public roads in the unincorporated area of the county shall be named without approval of the address program administrator with the concurrence of the board of commissioners. 
(b)  No new private road names shall be recognized by this article or added to the county's list of road names without prior approval of the address program administrator with the concurrence of the board of commissioners. 
(c)  The name of any new road, public or private, shall not duplicate or be confusingly similar to any other road name already named by this article or any subsequent ordinances or amendments thereto. This subsection shall not apply to an extension of existing roads. 
(d)  New subdivision roads, whether public or private, shall be named when created through the subdivision process which shall include submission of the road names to the address program administrator for approval. 
(e)  Developers establishing new public roads shall pay the county for the actual cost of purchasing and erecting street signs which meet the standards of the department of transportation. 
(f)  Developers desiring to use any type of sign, other than the style which meets standards set forth by the department of transportation, on a public road, shall have the style and design approved by the address program administrator with the concurrence of the board of commissioners. 
(g)  The names of private roads, including mobile home roads, which require naming to facilitate postal delivery and emergency response, shall be recognized by the county at the request of the citizens who own property adjacent to the road. Such road must serve at least three (3) households. The name of the private road shall be commonly known to the community. If there are two (2) or more recommendations of names for such road, the county will recognize the name preferred by at least fifty-one percent (51%) of the property owners on the road; however, this recognition shall not constitute acceptance of dedication of the road by the county for maintenance or other purposes. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 9, 12-7-1995) 
Sec. 38-73. - Numbers for future structures and lots. 
All residential and business buildings erected after the adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived shall be assigned a number prior to the issuance of a building permit. Owners shall purchase and display such number as provided in section 38-68. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 11, 12-7-1995) 
Sec. 38-74. - Utility company compliance. 
(a)  Following the adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived, all utility services regulated by the state public service commission, or any utility cooperative service organization providing service in the unincorporated area of the county, shall withhold service from any building, dwelling, mobile home or other structure not exempt under this article, until the owner or other requesting party has furnished the utility with a valid assigned number. 
(b)  It shall be the responsibility of the address program administrator to notify each affected utility of each implementation area by issuing maps and lists of official numbers assigned each structure or use. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 12, 12-7-1995) 
Sec. 38-75. - Implementations by county departments. 
Every department and official under the jurisdiction of the board of commissioners shall not render any nonemergency service until the occupant, owner or requesting individual has provided the department with a valid assigned number. Nonemergency service includes any service, except law enforcement, fire, rescue or emergency medical service. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 13, 12-7-1995) 
Sec. 38-76. - Renaming roads. 
The provisions of the Road Renaming Resolution adopted on July 6, 1993, shall be amended to provide as follows: 
(1)  Property owners who want to have the name of a road changed shall submit a petition to the address program administrator. The address program administrator will make recommendations to the board of commissioners after the following criteria have been met: 
a.  A nonrefundable fee as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the county clerk for each road shall accompany any petition requesting that an existing road name be changed. 
b.  The petition shall be in substantial conformity with the provisions of such resolution. 
c.  If the address program administrator approves the request, with the concurrence of the board of commissioners, the petitioners shall be required to pay the county for the cost of purchasing new signs and erecting such signs, including labor. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 10, 12-7-1995) 
Sec. 38-77. - Enforcement; penalty. 
Owners or occupants of buildings already constructed which do not comply with this article will be notified and requested to meet the requirements of this article within sixty (60) days from the date of notification. A warning notice will be issued after sixty (60) days if the requirements have not been met. The owner or occupant who does not voluntarily comply with this article within thirty (30) days after delivery of a warning notice by registered or certified mail shall be subject to criminal prosecution. Any person violating a provision of the county road addressing ordinance shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished by a fine as provided in section 1-19, and if such violation is continued, each day's violation shall be a separate offense. Violation of this article may also be enforced by seeking an order to compel compliance of civil remedies against the violator. Prosecutions for violation of the county road addressing ordinance shall be upon citation as provided in O.C.G.A. §§ 15-10-62 and 15-10-63 in the magistrate court of the county. The address program administrator is authorized to issue citations for the enforcement of the provisions of the county road naming and addressing ordinance in accordance with the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 15-10-63. 
(Ord. No. O-4-95, § 14, 12-7-1995) 
Secs. 38-78—38-85. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - UTILITY ACCOMMODATIONS IN RIGHTS-OF-WAY 

Sec. 38-86. - Title; definitions. 
(a)  This article shall be known as the "Dade County Utility Accommodations in Rights-of-Way Ordinance". 
(b)  As used in this article, unless the context clearly requires otherwise, the following words or phrases shall have the following meanings: 
Applicant means a person submitting all required information necessary for the director of public works to consider issuance of a permit to conduct excavation or construction activity within the public right-of-way or county road. 
Construction means the planning, location, surveying, designing, supervising, inspecting, paving, striping, modifying, grading, relocating, fixing, and the actual installation of a utility facility within the county road or county right-of-way. 
County means the unincorporated areas of Dade County, Georgia, and any division, department, agency, authority, instrumentality, or branch thereof, or the county governing authority, its board of commissioners, director of public works, or other county officers in charge of the roads, bridges and revenues of the county. 
County road means a highway, road, street, avenue, toll road, toll way, drive, detour, or other way open to the public, and intended for use for its enjoyment and for the passage of vehicles in the county, including but not limited to the following public rights, structures, sidewalks, facilities, and appurtenances incidental to the construction, maintenance, and enjoyment of such rights-of-way: surface, shoulders, and sides; bridges; causeways; viaducts; overpasses; underpasses; railroad grade crossings; tunnels; signs, signals, markings or other traffic control devices; way-side parks; parking facilities; drainage ditches; canals and culverts; and scenic easements and easements of light, air, view, and access. 
Damage means any impact or exposure that results in the need to repair utility facilities due to the weakening or the partial or complete destruction of a facility, including, but not limited to, the protective coating, lateral support, cathodic protection or the housing for the line, device, or facility. 
Permit means an authorization which grants permission to conduct specific regulated activities on, in, over, under or within the public right-of-way, in which a sub-condition set forth in this article and the permit document. 
Utility means all privately, publicly, or cooperatively owned systems for producing, transmitting, or distributing communication, data, information, telecommunication, cable television, power, electricity, light, heat, gas, oil, crude products, water/sewer, steam, fire and police signals, traffic control devices, and street lighting systems, and housing or conduit for any of the foregoing, which directly or indirectly serve the public or any part thereof. The term utility may also be used to refer to the owner, operator, provider, servicer, or any agent thereof, of any above-described utility or utility facility. 
Utility facilities means pipes, mains, conduits, cable wires, poles, towers, traffic and other signals, and other equipment, of any utility, in, on, along, over, or under the county roads or rights-of-way. 
(Ord. of 7-7-2005, § I) 
Sec. 38-87. - Standards for utility facilities in rights-of-way. 
(a)  Adopted . All utilities maintaining or locating their facilities on or in county roads or rights-of-way shall maintain or locate their facilities in accordance with the state department of transportation's utility accommodation policy and standards, as they may be amended from time to time and which are hereby adopted for all county roads and rights-of-way. A copy of the manual shall be maintained at the offices of the director of public works or his designee and the clerk of the board of commissioners, and shall be open for public inspection. 
(b)  Amendments . The 1988 Utility Accommodation Policy and Standards manual promulgated by the state department of transportation, as may be amended from time to time, adopted in subsection (a) of this section, is amended in order to equate state definitions and provisions with their appropriate and equivalent county counterparts, such that a policy shall be implemented to reflect the intent and effect of the state right-of- way policy as it would logically apply to county roads or rights-of-way, including, but not limited to the following: 
(1)  Commissioner = county director of public works; 
(2)  Department = county department (of public works); 
(3)  District engineer = county director of public works or his or her designee; 
(4)  Highway = any road that is part of the county road system; 
(5)  State = county; 
(6)  State bridge and structural design engineer = county director of public works or his or her designee; 
(7)  State highway (chief) engineer = county director of roads or his or her designee; 
(8)  State utilities engineer = county director of roads or his or her designee; 
(9)  Telephone booth = shall include any booth or structure, to be used by the public at large, which houses a communications link for local or long distance communications, including but not limited to data communication ports, terminals, kiosks, structures or jacks for connection with local or long distance communications; 
(10)  Utility = shall be defined as stated in § 38-86. 
(c)  Administration . The director of public works shall have the authority to administer the state department of transportation's utility accommodation policy and standards, as amended from time to time by the state or county, on county roads and rights-of-way in accordance with any policies and procedures the director of public works may establish hereunder and as approved by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 7-7-2005, § II) 
Sec. 38-88. - Permit required. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to install, construct, maintain, renew, remove, or relocate utility facilities in, on, along, over, or under county roads or rights-of-way without having first complied with all county ordinances regulating the use of county roads and rights-of-way and without having first applied for and received a utility permit from the director of public works allowing such utility usage of the county roads and rights-of-way. 
(b)  The director of public works shall adopt permitting policies and procedures, pursuant to approval by board of commissions, as deemed necessary to implement the requirements of this article. 
(c)  The board of commissioners shall be authorized to charge permit application fees in accordance with the state department of transportation's utility accommodations policy and standards and any other applicable laws that exist now or may be enacted in the future. Fees shall be determined by the director of the public works and subject to the approval of and publicly disclosed by the board of commissioners. Any fee schedule shall be posted at the offices of the director of public works or his designee and the clerk of the board of commissioners and open for public inspection. 
(d)  After work approved under this section has been completed, the utility shall repair the pavement, or portion of rights-of-way, that has been encroached upon. Repair work shall be completed in accordance with all of the work specifications on file with the director of public works and to the director's satisfaction. 
(e)  The rights-of-way shall be kept clear of any form of unnecessary obstruction. Anyone not having written permission from the director of public works to place any type of structure or material, including junk or debris, on the rights-of-way shall be subject to legal action and/or prosecution as provided by law. 
(f)  The issuance of a permit under this article is a license for a permissive use only and shall not be construed so as to give the grantee any permanent right or exclusive easement. A permit issued under this chapter shall only authorize that construction specifically shown in the application, and construction shall be in strict compliance with the plan submitted with the application, unless the county has granted an exception. 
(Ord. of 7-7-2005, § III) 
Sec. 38-89. - Facilities. 
Each utility with facilities located on county roads or rights-of-way shall furnish the department of roads with a map or drawing showing the county roads or rights-of-way on which the utility's facilities are located, and shall furnish the map or drawing within sixty (60) days if the same is requested by the director of public works. Each utility furnishing such map to the director of public works shall be entitled to receive notice from the director of public works before the issuance of any permit to another utility for construction work that might, in the opinion of the director of public works, effect the operations or services of the utility so notified. The applicant for any permit, upon request of any utility so notified, shall meet with such utility at the proposed location of construction work and review the proposed construction work as set out in the application. 
(Ord. of 7-7-2005, § IV) 
Sec. 38-90. - Removal, relocation or repair. 
(a)  The county shall have superior rights to the use of its public roads and public right-of-way. 
(b)  The county reserves the right to subsequently require any utility hereunder to remove, relocate, or repair the utility facility at the sole cost of the utility so that the county may make future improvements or operations in the county road system or any road right-of-way of the county road system, and each utility shall remove, relocate, or repair same as so requested by the county within sixty (60) days after receiving written notice with reference to the same from the county. Should the utility fail to remove, relocate, or repair any such utility facility, the county may so remove, relocate or repair the same and submit a statement of the total costs for the same to the utility. Within thirty (30) days of receiving such statement, the utility shall pay to the county the full cost of such removal, relocation or repairs. By the placement or maintenance of any utility facility hereunder, the utility agrees that in the event the utility fails or refuses to pay such costs incurred by the county for such removal, relocation or repairs, and it becomes necessary for the county to commence an action or proceeding in any court of competent jurisdiction to recover such cost, the county shall be entitled to recover, in addition to the statutory court costs and disbursements, such additional sums as the court may adjudge reasonable for attorneys' fees to be allowed the county in any such action or proceeding. 
(Ord. of 7-7-2005, § V) 
Sec. 38-91. - Liability for damages. 
(a)  Any and all damages to county roads or rights-of-way caused by a utility must be repaired immediately by the utility to the satisfaction of the director of public works. If satisfactory repairs are not made, any costs or expenses incurred by the county in repairing or replacing the structure which are not left in the original condition by the utility shall be chargeable to the utility, including reasonable attorneys' fees incurred in connection with such costs or expenses. The maintenance of a utility's facilities on county roads or rights-of-way shall be deemed as that utility's agreement to pay for such attorneys' fees as provided in this section. 
(b)  The county, its officers, employees, contractors, or other agents, shall not be held responsible or liable for injury or damage that may occur to facilities covered by a permit issued under this chapter, or to any connection or connections thereto, by reasons of road maintenance or construction activities or road contractors or utilities operations. The county, its officers, employees, contractors, or other agents shall not be held liable for any damages that may occur to utility facilities if the utility has been notified of the construction conflict and given reasonable time to mark or relocate its facilities and has failed to do so. 
(c)  The utility shall indemnify and hold harmless the county and all of the officers, employees, or other agents of the county, against any and all claims, damages, demands, actions, causes of death, costs and expenses, of whatever nature, which may result from any injury to or the death of any person(s) or from the loss of, or damage to, property of any kind or nature, if such injury, loss, or death arises out of the construction, operation, maintenance, repair, removal or relocation of facilities pursuant to a permit issued under this chapter. 
(Ord. of 7-7-2005, § VI) 
Sec. 38-92. - Violations; penalties; authority to stop work. 
If any provision of this chapter is violated, the county may cause all work to be stopped, the utility facility under construction to be removed, and the roadway to be repaired to its original condition. In addition to other remedies or penalties set forth in this article, any person, firm, corporation, association, partnership violating any provision of this chapter as the same exists or as it may hereinafter be amended, or shall fail to do anything required by this chapter as the same exists or as it may hereafter be amended, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, amenable to the process of the county magistrate court, and shall be punished as provided in § 1-19 of the county code of ordinances. In the event any provision of this chapter has been violated or is being violated, in addition to other remedies, the county may institute injunction, mandamus, or other appropriate action or proceeding to correct or abate such violation. 
(Ord. of 7-7-2005, § VII) 
Sec. 38-93. - Enforcement of other laws, rules, or regulations not limited; severability. 
This article shall not limit the authority of any state, local agency, or department of the county to enforce any other laws, rules, regulations or ordinances relating to utilities. In the event any section, subsection, sentence, clause, or phrase of this article is declared or adjudged to be unconstitutional, or otherwise contrary to law, such adjudication shall in no manner affect any other section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase, and shall remain in full force and effect as if the section, subsection, sentence, clause, or phrase so declared or adjudged invalid or unconstitutional, or not originally a part hereof. 
(Ord. of 7-7-2005, § VIII) 
Secs. 38-94—38-100. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - DRIVEWAY PIPE INSTALLATION 

Sec. 38-101. - Title; definitions. 
(a)  This article shall be known as the "Dade County Driveway Pipe Installation Ordinance". 
(b)  As used in this article, unless the context clearly requires otherwise, the following words or phrases shall have the following meanings: 
County means the unincorporated areas of Dade County, Georgia, and any division, department, agency, authority, instrumentality, or branch thereof, its board of commissioners, director of public works, or other county officers in charge of the roads, bridges, or rights-of-way of the county. 
Driveway includes any new ingress or egress to private or public property from a county road right-of-way, and shall include ingress or egress for temporary or permanent use. 
Permit means authorization from the county to connect a driveway to a county road right-of-way and/or to install driveway pipe on the county road rights-of-way. 
(Ord. No. 05-03-07, § I, 5-3-2007) 
Sec. 38-102. - Permit required; actions prohibited. 
(a)  A permit shall be required before connecting a driveway to county roads or before installing driveway pipe in the county road rights-of-way. This requirement shall be applicable to all driveways located in the county, whether the driveways be for residential, commercial, temporary, or permanent use, and shall include without limitation access driveways. 
(b)  Drainage ditches along county road rights-of-way shall not be temporarily filled for access to building sites. No debris, excavation, building materials or other such things shall be placed on the county right-of-way at the construction sites. 
(Ord. No. 05-03-07, § II, 5-3-2007) 
Sec. 38-103. - Permit conditions. 
A permit shall be issued under this article subject to the following terms: 
(1)  Applications for a permit for a driveway and/or driveway pipe installation shall be made with the county building official or public works department. 
(2)  The application shall include the name and telephone number of the applicant, the exact address or detailed description of the location for which access to the county road right-of-way is requested, and such other information as may be requested by for the public works director or county building official in the furtherance of the required duties under this article. 
(3)  The applicant shall be advised that two (2) inspection phases, as required by this article, shall be as follows: 
a.  Initial investigation of the site to determine the proper pipe size and installation procedures required; and 
b.  Final inspection prior to pouring or laying the permanent driveway surface. 
(Ord. No. 05-03-07, § III, 5-3-2007) 
Sec. 38-104. - Specifications for pipe installation. 
(a)  Prior to installation, all pipes to be installed on county road rights-of-way must be approved for use by the county. 
(b)  Pipe to be installed under this article must meet the following minimum requirements and such other characteristics as required by the county: 
(1)  All pipes shall be either class 3 reinforced concrete or corrugated metal. The public works department will determine which type pipe is to be installed on the initial inspection. 
(2)  Metal driveway pipe shall be a minimum of twelve-gauge galvanized corrugated pipe. 
(3)  The diameter of the pipe required is to be determined upon the initial site inspection by a representative from the public works department. 
(4)  Pipe culverts for residential driveways must be a minimum of twenty (20) feet in length, plus any additional length requirements due to special conditions such as ditches over two (2) feet in depth, high fills or other safety considerations. 
(5)  Arch pipe will be required when the depth of the ditch is not sufficient to handle standard round pipe. 
(6)  Pipe culverts for commercial driveways shall be determined individually to suit conditions, use and safety. 
(7)  The material used to cover pipes shall be required to be of a good grade of chert, sandy clay, or its equivalent, and shall be free from particles over two (2) inches in size. All cover materials shall be well compacted. 
(8)  The pipe shall be laid on a well-compacted true-to-line grade with a uniform bearing throughout the line. The line must have a minimum of one-tenth foot of fall per ten (10) feet. 
(Ord. No. 05-03-07, § IV, 5-3-2007) 
Sec. 38-105. - Enforcement; penalties for violations. 
(a)  If any provision of this article is violated, the county may cause all work to be stopped, the driveway pipe or other installation be removed from the county right-of-way, and the roadway be repaired to its' original condition. In addition to other remedies or penalties set forth in this article, any person, firm, corporation, association, or partnership violating any provision of this article as the same exists or as it may hereinafter be amended, or shall fail to do anything required by this article, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, amenable to the process of the county magistrate court, and shall be punished as provided in § 1-19 of the county code of ordinances. In the event any provision of this article has been violated or is being violated, in addition to other remedies, the county may institute an injunction, mandamus, or other appropriate action or proceeding to correct or date such violation. 
(b)  Any and all damages to county roads rights-of-way caused by violation of this article must be repaired immediately to the satisfaction of the director of public works. If satisfactory repairs are not made, any costs or expenses incurred by the county in repairing the county right-of-way shall be chargeable to any individuals or entity violating this article, including reasonable attorneys fees incurred in connection with such costs or expense. 
(Ord. No. 05-03-07, § V, 5-3-2007) 
Sec. 38-106. - Enforcement of other laws not limited; severability. 
This article shall not limit the authority of any state, local agency, or department of the county to enforce any other laws, rules, regulations, or ordinances. In the event any section, subsection, sentence, clause, or phrase of this article is declared or adjudged to be unconstitutional, or otherwise contrary to law, such adjudication shall in no manner affect any other section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase, and shall remain in full force and effect as if the section, subsection, sentence, clause or phase so declared or adjudged invalid or unconstitutional was not originally a part hereof. This article shall become effective immediately upon its adoption, and all ordinances in conflict with this article are repealed to the extent of the conflict. 
(Ord. No. 05-03-07, § VI, 5-3-2007) 
Chapter 42 - SIGNS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Signs, display of prices and inside sales of alcoholic beverages, § 6-40; buildings and building regulations, ch. 18. 
State Law reference— Control of signs and signals, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-50 et seq.; unlawful placement of signs within right-of-way of public road, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-51; outdoor advertising near state highways, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-70 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 42-1—42-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - INTERSTATE SIGNS 

Sec. 42-31. - Applicability. 
This article shall apply to all outdoor advertising signs in the county, abutting or visible from Interstate 24 and Interstate 59 rights-of-way. 
(Ord. of 2-22-1983, § I(1)) 
Sec. 42-32. - Compliance. 
No sign shall be erected or maintained unless it is in compliance with the regulations of this article. 
(Ord. of 2-22-1983, § I(2)) 
Sec. 42-33. - Construction; condition. 
Signs must be constructed of durable materials, maintained in good condition and shall not be permitted to become dilapidated. 
(Ord. of 2-22-1983, § I(3)) 
Sec. 42-34. - Conformance. 
All signs located on sites abutting or visible from Interstate 24 and Interstate 59 rights-of-way shall conform with the Georgia Outdoor Advertising Code, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-70 et seq., and shall meet all federal and state requirements necessary to obtain a permit under such code. In instances where the sign controls of this article are more strict, this article shall then apply. 
(Ord. of 2-22-1983, § I(4))
