(2)  Petroleum oil and other hydrocarbons, regardless of gravity, which are produced at the well in liquid form by ordinary production methods and which are not the result of condensation of gas after it leaves the reservoir. 
Person means an individual, trust, firm, joint stock company, corporation, including a government corporation, partnership, association, county, municipality, commission or political subdivision, or any agency of any other state or of the federal government. The county shall not be included within this definition of a "person." 
Private sanitary landfill means a disposal site not owned by a governmental entity, designed and employing engineering methods of disposing of solid wastes in a manner that minimizes environmental hazards by spreading, compacting to the smallest volume and applying cover material over all exposed material at the end of each operating day. 
Property owner means the person who has legal title to real estate located in the county. 
Screening means the use of any vegetative planting, fencing, ornamental wall of masonry or other architectural treatment or device, earthen embankment, or any combination thereof, which will effectively shield or buffer any activity or facility requiring a special use permit from adjoining tracts of land. 
Setback line means a line parallel to the property line in front of which no foundation wall or part of the structure of any building shall project with the exception of roof overhangs and the subsurface projection of footings. 
Significant groundwater recharge area means those areas mapped as such by the department of natural resources in the Hydrologic Atlas 18, 1989 edition. Mapping of recharge areas is based upon outcrop area, lithology, soil type and thickness, slope, density of lithologic contacts, geologic structure, the presence of karst and potentiometric surfaces. 
Solid waste means solid waste as defined by regulations promulgated by the administrator of the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency, pursuant to the federal act, which are in force and effect on February 1, 1991, codified as 40 CFR 261.1, 40 CFR 261.2(a)—(d) and 40 CFR 261.4(a). Solid waste also means discarded putrescible and nonputrescible waste, except water-carried body waste and recovered materials, and shall include garbage; rubbish, such as paper, cartons, boxes, wood, tin cans, glass, crockery or dunnage; ashes; street refuse; dead animals; sewage sludges; animal manure; industrial operations; residue from solid waste thermal treatment technology; food processing waste; demolition waste; abandoned automobiles; dredging waste; construction waste; and other waste material in a solid, semisolid or liquid state, not otherwise defined in this definition. Solid waste shall not include any material which is regulated pursuant to the Georgia Water Quality Control Act, O.C.G.A. tit. 12, ch. 5, art. 2 or the Georgia Air Quality Control Act of 1978, O.C.G.A. tit. 12, ch. 9. 
Special solid waste means any solid waste not otherwise regulated under the Georgia Hazardous Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. tit. 12, ch. 8, art. 3 and regulations promulgated under such article originating or produced from or by a source or generator not subject to regulation under O.C.G.A. § 12-8-22. 
Spill or release means the discharge, deposit, injection, dumping, spilling, emitting, releasing, leaking or placing of any substance requiring a special use permit by any person or from any property under the ownership or control of that person into the air or into or on any land or water, including groundwater, of the county, except as specifically authorized in the special use permit pertaining to that person regardless of the state of mind of such person with respect to such occurrence and regardless of ultimate liability for such occurrence. Accidental discharges of oil made by a person during maintenance of that person's personal vehicle or farm machinery shall be exempt, provided the activity engaged in by that person prior to the discharge is otherwise exempt. 
Start of construction , for other than new construction or substantial improvements under the Coastal Barrier Resources Act, PL 97-348), includes substantial improvement, and means the date the building permit was issued, provided the actual start of construction, repair, reconstruction or improvement was within 360 days of the building permit date. The actual start of construction means the first placement of permanent construction of a structure, including a manufactured home, on a site, such as the pouring of slabs or footings, installation of piles, construction of columns or any work beyond the stage of excavation or the placement of a manufactured home on a foundation. Permanent construction does not include land preparation, such as clearing, grading and filling; nor does it include excavation for a basement, footings, piers or foundations or the erection of temporary forms; nor does it include the installation on the property of accessory buildings, such as garages or sheds not occupied as dwelling units or not part of the main structure. 
Storage means the containment or holding of hazardous waste, either on a temporary basis or for a period of years, in such a manner as not to constitute disposal of such hazardous waste. 
Structure means anything constructed or erected, the use of which requires location on the ground or attachment to something having location on the ground, and also includes manufactured homes, gas or liquid storage tanks or other manmade facilities or infrastructures, but does not include fences. 
Variance means a grant of relief from the requirements of this article which permits construction in a manner otherwise prohibited by this article where specific enforcement of this article would result in an unnecessary hardship. 
Water supply watershed means the area of land upstream of a governmentally owned public drinking water intake or water supply reservoir. 
Wetlands means those areas that are inundated or saturated by surface or groundwater at a frequency and duration sufficient to support, and under normal circumstances do or would support, a prevalence of vegetative or aquatic life typically adapted for life, growth and reproduction in saturated or seasonally saturated soil conditions. Wetlands generally include swamps, marshes, bogs and similar areas such as sloughs, potholes, wet meadows, river overflows, mud flats and natural ponds. The ecological parameters for designating wetlands include hydric soils, hydrophytic vegetation and hydrological conditions that involve a temporary or permanent source of water to cause soil saturation. The term "wetlands" shall be further defined by 33 CFR 32.93, the Federal Manual for Identifying and Delineating Wetlands, and Criteria for Wetlands Protection ch. 391-3-16.03 of the rules of the state department of natural resources, environmental division. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.07) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 46-37. - Abrogation. 
This article is not intended to repeal, abrogate or interfere with any existing easements, covenants or deed restrictions duly recorded in the public records of the county. Nothing in this article shall be construed to give the board of commissioners the responsibility for enforcing private covenants or deed restrictions. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.08) 
Sec. 46-38. - When special use permit required; application; issuance. 
(a)  Uses and facilities controlled in this article are prohibited unless and until a special use permit is first obtained from the special use permit board. 
(b)  An application for a special use permit shall be submitted to the special use permit board on such forms and in such manner as the special use permit board may prescribe and shall be accompanied by an application fee as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the county clerk. 
(c)  A special use permit shall be issued to an applicant on evidence, satisfactory to the special use permit board, of compliance with all applicable provisions of this article. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.09) 
Sec. 46-39. - Unlawful practices. 
Without first obtaining and possessing a special use permit, it shall be unlawful and a violation of this article to: 
(1)  Engage in the disposal of any biomedical waste, contaminant, designated hazardous waste, hazardous chemical substance or mixture, hazardous constituent, hazardous waste, municipal solid waste, oil, pesticide, solid waste or special solid waste. 
(2)  Construct, install, operate or substantially alter any composting facility, land disposal facility, landfill, municipal solid waste disposal facility, municipal solid waste landfill, private sanitary landfill or incinerator. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.10) 
Sec. 46-40. - Information required for a special use permit. 
(a)  Any person, entity or organization desiring to apply for a special use permit must provide the following information: 
(1)  If the applicant, permit holder or any owner of the proposed use or facility is a corporation, proof shall be submitted that any such corporation is in good standing with the state. 
(2)  The names and addresses of all persons having a legal or equitable ownership interest of at least one percent (1%) in the business or enterprise proposing the use or facility. 
(3)  If either the applicant, permit holder or any owner of the proposed use or facility is a corporation, the names and addresses of all officers and directors of such corporation. 
(4)  If either the applicant, permit holder or any owner of the proposed use or facility is a corporation, the name and address of the registered agent for service of process and notices shall be stated. 
(5)  State whether the applicant, permit holder or any owner, director or officer has ever been convicted of a felony, and, if so, provide details, including, but not limited to, a certified copy of the conviction. 
(6)  State whether the applicant, permit holder, owner or any director or officer has ever been charged, cited or had suit brought against him/her for violation of any law, rule, regulation or order relating to the protection of the environment, and, if so, provide details, including, but not limited to, a certified copy of the citation, suit or notice of violation. 
(7)  Submit a detailed list of all judgments, whether under appeal or not, which have been issued against the person or organization seeking the special use permit during the previous seven (7) years, whether or not in the state. 
(8)  Submit a detailed list of all litigation involving the person or organization seeking the special use permit during the previous seven (7) years, whether or not in the state. 
(9)  Submit copies of all state and federal income tax returns for the owner, applicant and/or the permit holder, for the three (3) years preceding the filing of the application for a special use permit. 
(10)  Submit a current audited financial statement, prepared according to generally accepted accounting principles, of the applicant, permit holder and/or owner, showing assets, liabilities, income, expenditures and a budget for the current year. 
(11)  Submit a detailed list of all facilities that the applicant, owner and/or permit holder owns, operates or uses, which are similar in character to the use or facility for which the application has been made. 
(12)  State whether or not the applicant, permit holder, owner and/or any officer or director thereof has ever been denied a permit for a use or facility, or proposed use or facility, similar in character to the use or facility for which application has been made, and, if so, provide a written copy of the denial and state the name, address and telephone number of the person or entity which was denied such permit. 
(13)  Provide certified copies of all necessary applications and permits, licenses and approvals from state and federal environmental regulatory agencies for the use or facility for which the application is being made. 
(14)  Provide a detailed list of materials identified in section 46-39 which are anticipated to be stored or handled at the facility. For each such item listed, any known deleterious medical effects must be stated and copies supplied to any entity located in the county which renders medical care and to any ambulance service operating within the county. 
(15)  The application shall be accompanied by three (3) certified plats, prepared by a state registered land surveyor, drawn to scale, showing the proposed location of the various different uses of the property, the boundary lines of the property, the dimensions of the property, the names and addresses of the owners of all adjacent properties, the location of all existing county roads which abut the property, the location of all proposed drives, roads, parking facilities and structures to be located on the property and any measurements, illustrating compliance with the setback, screening and other provisions contained in this article. 
(16)  The application shall also include a topographical map and grading plan, the type and location of drainage and sewerage, water, electrical, gas and other utilities to serve the proposed facility. 
(17)  The applicant must also include with the application a specific, detailed emergency operational plan developed in conjunction with the county emergency management agency, which states measures to be taken if a loss of containment of any of the materials which are anticipated to be stored occurs. This plan shall anticipate the orderly evacuation of surrounding residents, if necessary. 
(b)  The special use permit board may require such other plans, data, specifications, engineering reports, designs and other information it deems necessary, at the cost of the applicant, to make a determination of compliance with this article. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.11) 
Sec. 46-41. - Initial determination of application; denial. 
(a)  Upon receipt of an application for a special use permit, the special use permit board shall, within forty-five (45) days, make a determination as to whether the minimum requirements of this article have been met. 
(b)  If the special use permit board finds that the application, as submitted, would preclude the issuance of a special use permit, then it may deny the application. The notice of denial shall state the reason for the denial. The notice shall further state the denial shall become final unless a written request for a hearing is filed with the special use permit board within fifteen (15) days from the date of such notice. The notice shall be delivered to the applicant either personally or by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.12) 
Sec. 46-42. - Weighing of advantages and disadvantages in making final determination; applicability to certain sensitive environments. 
(a)  Before a special use permit can be granted, the special use permit board must find, after a public hearing in accordance with section 46-43, that the public benefits of, and need for, the proposed use or facility are greater than any negative effects upon and risks to the environment, public health and safety. 
(b)  The special use permit board shall give careful consideration to any reasonably foreseeable negative effects upon, and risks to, the environment and public health and safety for a use or facility that is or would be located within a significant groundwater recharge area, wetland or water supply watershed. The special use permit board may order such studies and investigations, at the cost of the applicant, as the special use permit board may deem necessary to make such determination. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.13) 
Sec. 46-43. - Publication of notice of application; posting of sign; location and time of hearing. 
(a)  Within fifteen (15) days after the initial approval of an application for a special use permit, the special use permit board shall cause a notice of such application to be published in at least one (1) local newspaper of general circulation in the county, once a week for four (4) consecutive weeks, which notice shall state, at a minimum, that an application for a specified use or facility has been received, the name of the applicant, the date, time and location of a public hearing before the special use permit board and that the hearing shall be held for the purpose of receiving comments and suggestions concerning the location and requirements for the operation of the use or facility. 
(b)  The special use permit board shall, within fifteen (15) days of the initial approval of an application for a special use permit, cause to be posted a sign at or near the main entrance to the proposed site, visible from the public roadway at such entrance, stating substantially the same information as required by subsection (a) of this section. 
(c)  The hearing shall be held after the final publication of such notice of application for a special use permit, but not more than forty-five (45) days after the first publication of such notice. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.14) 
Sec. 46-44. - Conditions of issuance. 
(a)  A special use permit may be issued, provided that all of the following conditions are met: 
(1)  Adequate space for off-street parking shall be provided. 
(2)  A seven hundred fifty-yard setback buffer distance shall be maintained from the nearest corner of the nearest dwelling or structure intended for use as a dwelling, whether actually occupied or not. 
(3)  A five hundred-yard setback buffer distance shall be maintained from the nearest building line of a nondwelling building or structure used for human occupancy, such as businesses, industrial buildings, commercial offices, etc. 
(4)  A two hundred fifty-yard setback buffer distance shall be maintained from private property lines for aesthetic purposes. 
(5)  Other provisions of any zoning ordinance, including, but not limited to, type of zoning at the site, setback buffers and screening, applying to the particular use and the type of use shall be complied with. 
(6)  The proposed use shall not occur within a two-mile radius of any significant groundwater recharge area. 
(7)  The proposed use must be capable of being served by adequate public utilities. 
(8)  Adequate traffic routes and entrances must be established, including consideration of the deterioration of the existing roadway, expenditure of public funds to maintain roadways, adequacy and safety of road intersections, road widths on roads within and leading to the property, pavement conditions (material, thickness, age, etc.), width and length of property boundaries at road access areas and type of vehicles that may be used on the property. 
(9)  The lot size must be sufficient in order to provide the operational space needed for the proposed use or facility to carry out all business related transactions without infringing on setback and other requirements of this article. 
(10)  The owner and/or permit holder must provide adequate screening of the entire premises. The screening must effectively screen the premises on a yearround basis and must be compatible with the facility's surroundings. All screening must meet the criteria set forth in section 46-51. 
(11)  The owner and/or permit holder must provide proof that the use or facility shall not be located in an area which would be subject to a 100-year flood. 
(12)  Once the special use permit board has determined that all of the requirements of subsections (1)—(11) of this subsection have been satisfied, it must further find that the benefits of, and need for, the proposed use are greater than any possible depreciating effects and damages to the neighboring properties before a special use permit for such uses can be granted. 
(b)  Each special use permit shall contain such terms and conditions as are deemed necessary by the special use permit board to protect the environment, public health and safety. The special use permit board may require such testing and construction supervision as it deems necessary to protect the environment and public health and safety. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.15) 
Sec. 46-45. - Special use permit related fees. 
(a)  The owner or operator of any activity or facility requiring a special use permit, including an activity or facility granted interim status, shall pay, as a condition of such special use permit, fees, in addition to the application fee, sufficient to cover the reasonable costs and expenses of: 
(1)  Reviewing and acting upon any application for a special use permit or renewal thereof; 
(2)  Implementing and enforcing the terms of the special use permit; 
(3)  Notices required by this article; 
(4)  Monitoring, investigation and enforcement of activities and facilities requiring special use permits; 
(5)  Preparing generally applicable regulations and guidance; 
(6)  Modeling, analyses and demonstrations; and 
(7)  All other expenses of the special use permit board in connection with this article and related federal, state and local laws, rules, regulations and orders. 
(b)  The fee shall be as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the county clerk per ton or volume equivalent of substances received by a site or facility for disposal under this article. All fees shall be paid monthly. 
(c)  All fees collected under this section shall be paid into the county general fund. 
(d)  Fees under this section may not be assessed prior to September 1, 1995, against the holder of a valid special use permit with interim status. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.16) 
Sec. 46-46. - Duration and renewal of special use permits. 
(a)  Each special use permit shall have a duration of one (1) year. 
(b)  The holder of each special use permit may seek renewal of a special use permit by submitting to the special use permit board an application for renewal on such forms as may be prescribed by the special use permit board not more than sixty (60) nor less than thirty (30) days before the expiration of the special use permit, along with a fee for renewal in the amount as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the county clerk. 
(c)  The special use permit board shall conduct such inspections and investigations as it may deem necessary or useful in determining whether to renew a special use permit. 
(d)  The special use permit board shall not be required to renew the special use permit of an activity or facility that is not in full compliance with this article and all applicable federal, state and local laws, rules, regulations and orders. 
(e)  If the special use permit board denies an application for renewal, it shall send written notice of such denial to the permit holder setting forth in the notice the reason for such denial. Such notice shall state that the denial will become final unless a written request for a hearing is filed with the special use permit board within fifteen (15) days from the date of such notice. The notice shall be delivered to the permit holder either personally or by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.17) 
Sec. 46-47. - Application for modification of special use permit. 
(a)  Any permit holder may file an application for amendment or modification of a special use permit with the special use permit board. All modifications of existing special use permits shall be classified by the special use permit board as major or minor modifications. All modifications of existing special use permits to allow vertical or horizontal expansion of existing disposal facilities shall be classified as major permit modifications. Upon receipt of an application for a major permit modification, the procedures of this article shall be followed as if an original permit were sought. A modification may be granted only in accordance with this article. 
(b)  An application for amendment for a special use permit shall be submitted on such forms as may be prescribed by the special use permit board and shall be accompanied by an application fee as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges on file in the office of the county clerk. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.18) 
Sec. 46-48. - Financial responsibility. 
No special use permit shall be issued to any person, and no facility requiring a special use permit shall be constructed, operated, maintained, modified or sold by any person, unless such person can demonstrate financial responsibility for taking corrective action and for compensating a third party for bodily injury and/or property damage in an annual aggregate amount of five million dollars ($5,000,000.00). The required annual aggregate coverage amount shall not be deemed in any way to limit the liability of the owner or the operator. The owner or operator may use a surety bond and/or an irrevocable letter of credit to demonstrate financial responsibility. An owner or operator must maintain evidence of all financial assurance mechanisms used to demonstrate financial responsibility until released from the requirements of this section by the special use permit board. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.19) 
Sec. 46-49. - Interim status. 
(a)  Any person who owns or operates a facility required to have a special use permit, which facility was in existence prior to the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived, shall be deemed as having been issued an interim status special use permit, provided that such person notifies the special use permit board of the existence of such use or facility and general character thereof. Such notification may be in plain language and shall not require technical specificity, however, it shall be substantially accurate. 
(b)  Interim status for any use or facility required to file an application under this article shall expire within one (1) year of the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived. 
(c)  The maintenance of interim status shall require full compliance with all county, state and federal laws, statutes, rules, regulations and orders, regardless of whether environmentally related in their nature. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.20) 
Sec. 46-50. - Exempt activities; disposal of livestock feeding facility waste. 
(a)  A special use permit shall not be required for the following persons and activities, provided that federal and state laws are complied with and the activity does not adversely affect the natural resources or public health and safety of the county: 
(1)  Any individual disposing of solid waste originating from his own residence onto land or facilities owned by that individual; 
(2)  Individuals, farmers and other persons using pesticides and fertilizer on land under their ownership or control for the purpose of regulating and promoting plant growth; 
(3)  Existing facilities, sites and activities otherwise requiring a special use permit that are owned or operated by the county or the municipal corporation of Trenton, or the state; 
(4)  Incinerators at retail facilities and those used for religious ceremonies or crematorium purposes; 
(5)  Incinerators and composting used for agricultural purposes or poultry house operations; and 
(6)  Facilities which are shortterm collection and storage points for waste oil destined for recycling facilities located outside the county, provided such storage facility meets the requirements of O.C.G.A. § 12-13-1 et seq., where applicable. 
(b)  A special use permit shall not be required for a person disposing of livestock-feeding facility waste from his own facility with a maximum total capacity of one thousand (1,000) cattle or five thousand (5,000) swine, provided that such activity does not adversely affect the natural resources or public health or safety of the county. If such person shall provide an approved waste disposal system which is capable of properly disposing of the runoff from a ten-year storm, such person shall be further exempt regardless of total per head capacity. Nothing in this subsection shall limit the right of any person to use poultry or other animal manure for fertilizer; nor shall any part of this article be construed to limit any person's or organization's right to file a suit for nuisance against any person engaged in such enterprises. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.21) 
Cross reference— Animals, ch. 14. 
Sec. 46-51. - Screening. 
(a)  A special use permit may be issued, provided, in addition to all other conditions, that the following conditions are met: 
(1)  Screening criteria. 
a.  The screening shall be located on the owner's land and not on any part of the highway or road right-of-way. 
b.  The screening shall be in place prior to the time any hazardous materials are brought upon the premises. 
c.  At no time after the screen is established shall any hazardous materials be stacked high enough to be visible above the screen. No hazardous materials shall be placed outside the screen. 
d.  No hazardous materials shall be placed closer than fifty (50) feet to any highway or road right-of-way or any adjoining property line. 
e.  Fences must be located in such a manner as not to lessen visibility for the traveling public utilizing the public roads, nor to be a hazard or danger to the traveling public. 
f.  The construction of fences shall be uniform and no patchwork type of construction shall be permitted. 
g.  When fences are painted, the paint used shall be of a color so as to blend into the environs of the highway or road right-of-way. 
h.  The fence enclosing the premises shall not be used for advertising purposes, except that a space no larger than six (6) feet by twelve (12) feet may be used to advertise the business. 
i.  The side lot lines must be screened if any hazardous material storage would be visible from the highway or road. 
j.  Facilities proposed to be established subsequent to this article, which are located on hills or valleys, which cannot be adequately screened, shall not be permitted. 
k.  The maximum height of any required fencing shall not exceed eight (8) feet. 
(2)  Acceptable fencing materials. Acceptable fencing shall include fences of steel or other metals, durable woods such as heart cypress, redwood or other wood treated with a preservative, or walls of masonry. Some of the types of fencing acceptable are as follows: 
a.  Chainlink with aluminum, steel, plastic or wooden slat inserts. 
b.  Wooden types of basket weave, palisade, louver or other suitable design. 
c.  Walls of masonry, including plain or ornamental concrete block, block, brick, stone or other suitable material. 
d.  An earth wall, if properly designed, grassed and landscaped. 
(3)  Plant material. All plant material shall be predominantly evergreen. The minimum size of plant material at the time of planting shall be as follows: 
a.  Evergreen shrubs: One and one-half (1½) feet to three (3) feet in height. 
b.  Evergreen trees: Four (4) feet to five (5) feet in height (pinus, Magnolia). 
c.  Small trees: Four (4) feet to five (5) feet in height (Hawthorn, Crepe Myrtle). 
d.  Large trees, deciduous: One (1) inch to one and one-half (1½) inches caliper (Maples, Sycamore, Sweetgum). 
(4)  Maintenance. The owner of any premises shall maintain the screening and shall do such painting and repairs as may be necessary to keep fences, walls or other structural material in good appearance. Plant material shall be maintained in a good, healthy condition. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.21) 
Sec. 46-52. - Grant of variance. 
(a)  Unless otherwise prohibited by state or federal law, the special use permit board may grant a variance from the rules and regulations governing special use permits if the special use permit board makes a finding that compliance with any provision would: 
(1)  Result in an arbitrary and unreasonable taking of property; 
(2)  Result, in effect, in the closing and elimination of any lawful business, occupation or activity without sufficient corresponding benefit or advantage to the public; 
(3)  Cause an unnecessary and material hardship; 
(4)  Not substantially further the purposes of this article because of extraordinary and exceptional conditions pertaining to the particular piece of property in question because of its size, shape or topography, or for other reasons; or 
(5)  Not substantially further the purposes of this article considering other relevant factors, provided that no variance shall be granted where such variance would permit the continuation of a condition which poses an undue present or potential threat to the environment or to the public health and safety; and provided, further, that any variance so granted shall not be construed to relieve any person from any liability imposed by any law, rule, order or regulation. 
(b)  Any person seeking a variance must file a request for a hearing in writing to the special use permit board. 
(c)  If the special use permit board denies a request for a variance, the notice of denial shall state the reason for the denial. The notice shall further state that the denial shall become final unless a request for a hearing is filed with the special use permit board within fifteen (15) days from the date of such notice. The notice shall be delivered to the person seeking the variance either personally or by certified mail, return receipt requested. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.22) 
Sec. 46-53. - Maintenance of records. 
The special use permit board may require the holder of a special use permit to maintain and submit records of the operation and maintenance of the use or facility concerning any matter material to this article. All such records shall be maintained on-site and shall be available for inspection by the special use permit board or its agents, upon reasonable notice. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.23) 
Sec. 46-54. - Assignability and transferability of special use permits. 
(a)  All special use permits, including, but not limited to, interim status permits, are nonassignable and nontransferable. Any attempt to transfer or assign a special use permit, including, but not limited to, an interim status permit, whether temporarily or permanently, and whether or not with reservation of rights, shall be sufficient grounds for revocation of the special use permit and shall constitute a criminal violation of this article. Any sale, lease or transfer of control of a use or facility holding a special use permit or an interim status permit from the entity possessing the special use permit or interim status permit prior to the issuance of a new permit allowing such sale, lease or transfer, shall also be sufficient grounds for revocation of the special use permit or interim status permit and shall also constitute a criminal violation of this article. For the purpose of this section, the sale of a controlling interest in stock in a corporation owning or possessing a special use permit or interim status permit shall constitute an assignment or transfer of such special use permit or interim status permit. 
(b)  If the special use permit board has cause to believe that a special use permit has been assigned or transferred, or that a facility requiring a special use permit has been sold, leased or has had control over it transferred, or that any such activity is about to occur, it may immediately or at any time seek appropriate equitable and injunctive relief. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.24) 
Sec. 46-55. - Inspection and investigation. 
(a)  The special use permit board or its authorized representative or agent, upon presentation of proper credentials, shall have the power to enter at reasonable times upon any private or public property for the purpose of inspection and investigation of conditions relating to this article. 
(b)  The special use permit board or its authorized representative, upon presentation of credentials, shall have a right to enter upon, into or through the premises of all persons or organizations subject to this article, or premises whereon a violation of this article is reasonably believed to be occurring or is reasonably believed to be about to occur, to investigate, take samples, take photographs and/or video or audio recordings, copy all records relating to this article and the purposes thereof, and inspect, for compliance with the requirements imposed under this article, to determine whether such a violation or threatened violation exists for the purpose of: 
(1)  Determining whether any person or organization subject to the requirements of this article is in compliance with any standard or requirement imposed pursuant to this article; 
(2)  Investigating conditions and activities when the special use permit board is in possession of information sufficient to form a reasonable belief that a violation of this article is occurring or is about to occur; or 
(3)  Determining whether there has been a violation of any of the provisions of this article or any permit issued pursuant thereto. 
(c)  Each inspection or investigation shall be commenced and completed with reasonable promptness. If the special use permit board or its authorized representative or agent obtains any samples prior to leaving the premises, such representative or agent shall give to the owner, operator, permit holder or agent in charge a receipt describing the sample obtained, and upon request, a portion of each sample in equal volume or weight to the portion retained. If any analysis is made of such samples, a copy of the result of such analysis shall be furnished promptly to the owner, operator, permit holder or agent in charge. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.25) 
Sec. 46-56. - Applicability to subject matter and other ordinances. 
This article shall apply to all subject matter that is regulated both by this article and other ordinances, including, but not limited to, ordinances for the development and maintenance of land; and such other ordinances are amended to reflect this. The board of commissioners may attach statements to such other ordinances to the effect that compliance with this article is required by such other ordinances. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.30) 
Sec. 46-57. - Conflict with other laws. 
Whenever the provisions and requirements of this article, or of any rule, regulation or order pursuant to this article, are more restrictive than those under any other statute, law, rule, regulation, ordinance or order of the county, the state or the United States, the provisions and requirements of this article, then the rules, regulations and orders pursuant to this article shall govern to the extent permissible by law. Whenever the provisions of any other statute, law, rule, regulation, ordinance or order of the county, the state or the United States are more restrictive than this article, or any other statute, law, rule, regulation or order pursuant to this article, then the provisions of such other statute, law, rule, regulation, ordinance or order shall govern. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.31) 
Sec. 46-58. - County not guarantor of acts or omissions of other entities. 
No act or omission of the county or of the special use permit board shall be an assurance or guarantee that the United States, or any department or agency thereof, or the state, or any department or agency thereof, or any other county or municipality, or any department or agency of any other county or municipality, has taken, is taking or will take any action, or has made, is making or will make any omission. No act or omission of the county or the special use permit board shall be construed as the rendering of advice or an opinion as to the status of legal requirements, policies, acts or omissions of any of the other entities set forth in this section. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.33) 
Sec. 46-59. - Personal service of notice. 
The county board of commissioners or the special use permit board may serve, or cause to be served, copies of this article upon any person or organization believed to be an owner or operator of a facility or activity subject to this article. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.34) 
Sec. 46-60. - Criminal acts; continuing offenses; penalties; jurisdiction over offenses. 
(a)  The following are declared to be unlawful and criminal acts, notwithstanding other provisions of this article: 
(1)  It shall be unlawful to engage in any activity in violation of applicable requirements, rules, regulations, permit conditions and orders established under this article. 
(2)  It shall be a criminal violation of this article to furnish false or materially incomplete or misleading information to the special use permit board or a lawful designee of the special use permit board, on any application, investigation or proceeding regarding special use permits. 
(b)  Each day that a violation of this article continues shall be deemed a separate offense. At the discretion of the presiding judge, a violator of this article may be given a reasonable length of time to rectify or correct such violation. 
(c)  Jurisdiction over offenses under this article shall be in the county magistrate court. Any person violating the terms of this article or any permit condition, rule or regulation promulgated pursuant thereto, may be punished as provided in section 1-19, for each offense. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.35) 
Sec. 46-61. - Civil action by private citizens. 
Nothing in this article shall prevent an adjacent or neighboring property owner who is damaged by a violation of this article, or any other person who would have standing, to bring a civil action for damages, injunctive relief, to abate a nuisance, for a writ of mandamus or other appropriate relief. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.36) 
Sec. 46-62. - Amendments. 
If the board of commissioners desires to take action resulting in the adoption of an amendment to this article, it shall provide for a public hearing on the proposed action. At least fifteen (15) days, but not more than forty-five (45) days, prior to the date of the hearing, the board of commissioners shall cause to be published in a newspaper of general circulation, within the territorial boundaries of the county, a notice of the hearing, stating the time, place and purpose of the hearing. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.37) 
Sec. 46-63. - Appeals of decisions. 
All decisions of the special use permit board may be appealed to the county board of commissioners. The appeal process shall be governed by the rules and regulations set out in this article. 
(Ord. of 9-7-1993, § 1.38) 
Secs. 46-64—46-95. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - LITTER CONTROL[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Litter Control Law, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-40 et seq.; littering highways, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-249. 

Sec. 46-96. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Litter means all sand, gravel, slag, brickbats, rubbish, waste material, used tires, refuse, garbage, trash, debris, dead animals or discarded materials of every kind and description. 
Public or private property means the right-of-way of any road or highway and county waste transfer station, and body of water or watercourse thereof, any park, playground, building, refuge or conservation or recreation area, and residential or farm properties, timberlands or forests. 
(Ord. of 1-3-1992, § 1-3) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 46-97. - Littering. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to dump, deposit, throw or leave, or to cause or permit the dumping, depositing, placing, throwing or leaving, of litter on any public or private property in the county, or any waters in the county, unless the: 
(1)  Property is designated by the county, or political subdivisions located within the county, for the disposal of litter, and the person is authorized by the proper public authority to use such property; 
(2)  Litter is placed into a litter receptacle or container installed on such property; or 
(3)  Person is the owner or tenant in lawful possession of such property, or has first obtained consent of the owner or tenant in lawful possession, or unless the act is done under the personal direction of the owner or tenant, all in a manner consistent with the public welfare. 
(Ord. of 1-3-1992, § 1-4) 
Sec. 46-98. - Punishment. 
Any person who violates section 46-97, upon conviction thereof, shall be punished as follows: 
(1)  By a fine as provided in section 1-19; 
(2)  In the sound discretion of a court in which conviction is obtained, the person may be directed to pick up and remove from any public street, highway or right-of-way, for a distance not to exceed one (1) mile, any litter he/she has deposited and any and all litter deposited thereon by anyone else prior to the date of execution of such sentence; or 
(3)  In the sound discretion of the judge of a court in which conviction is obtained, the person may be directed to pick up and remove from any public beach, public park, private right-of-way or, with the prior permission of the legal owner or tenant in lawful possession of such property, and private property upon which it can be established by competent evidence that he/she has deposited litter, any and all litter deposited thereon by anyone prior to the date of execution of such sentence. 
(Ord. of 1-3-1992, § 1-5) 
Sec. 46-99. - Prima facie evidence; rebuttable presumption. 
(a)  Whenever litter is thrown, deposited, dropped or dumped from any motor vehicle, boat, airplane or other conveyance in violation of section 46-97, it shall be prima facie evidence that the operator of the conveyance has violated this article. 
(b)  Except as provided in subsection (a) of this section, whenever any litter which is dumped, deposited, thrown or left on public or private property in violation of this article, is discovered to contain any article, including, but not limited to, letters, bills, publications or other writings which display the name of a person thereon in such a manner as to indicate that the article belonged to such person, it shall be a rebuttable presumption that such person has violated this article. 
(Ord. of 1-3-1992, § 1-6) 
Sec. 46-100. - Enforcement. 
All law enforcement agencies, officers and officials of the state, or any political subdivision thereof, or any enforcement agency, officer or any official of any commission of the state, or any political subdivision thereof, is authorized, empowered and directed to enforce this article. 
(Ord. of 1-3-1992, § 1-7) 
Secs. 46-101—46-130. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - DUMPSTERS 

Sec. 46-131. - Applicability. 
The provisions of this article shall apply to all the unincorporated areas of the county and to any incorporated area of the county where the county maintains a dumpster for the use of county residents. 
(Ord. No. O-3-95, § 1.02, 7-6-1995) 
Sec. 46-132. - Purpose and findings. 
The disposal of common household waste or garbage of the residents of the county is of critical concern. The county currently owns and maintains dumpsters located throughout the county for the receipt of common household waste or garbage. Expenses related to the purchase of dumpsters and disposal areas and their maintenance, together with transportation costs and fees paid at landfills by the county, make it necessary and essential for the county to closely monitor and regulate the use of county dumpsters. Such regulation is necessary to maintain and improve the quality of life in the county and to protect the environment and property of the county and the health, safety and welfare of the citizens of the county. 
(Ord. No. O-3-95, § 1.03, 7-6-1995) 
Sec. 46-133. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Common household waste means any solid waste generated or derived from everyday household use, including garbage and trash from single-family or multifamily residences, but specifically excluding, without limitation, the following: 
(1)  Tires; 
(2)  Furniture; 
(3)  Appliances; 
(4)  Carpet; 
(5)  Construction debris; 
(6)  Batteries; 
(7)  Gas, oil or other petroleum products or byproducts; 
(8)  Brush; 
(9)  Leaves; 
(10)  Dead animals; 
(11)  Any contents or matter from any septic tank, wastewater holding tank or grease trap; 
(12)  Any commercial or industrial solid waste; 
(13)  Yard trimmings or solid waste from landscaping, gardening or agricultural activities; or 
(14)  Waste from home commercial activities. 
Dumpster means any container placed in the county by the county board of commissioners for the receipt of common household waste. 
Recovered materials mean those materials which have a known use, reuse or recycling potential; can be feasibly used, reused or recycled; and have been diverted or removed from the solid waste stream for sale, use, reuse or recycling, whether or not requiring subsequent separation and processing. 
Recovered materials processing facility means a facility engaged solely in the storage, processing and resale or reuse of recovered materials. 
Resident means any person residing in a single-family or multifamily residence located in the county. 
(Ord. No. O-3-95, § 1.05, 7-6-1995) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 46-134. - Unlawful acts. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person: 
(1)  Who is a resident, to directly or indirectly dump, place or otherwise deposit any matter into a county dumpster other than common household waste. 
(2)  Who is not a resident, to directly or indirectly dump, place or otherwise deposit any matter, including common household waste, into a county dumpster. 
(3)  To directly or indirectly dump, place or otherwise deposit any common household waste, or any matter other than recovered materials, into a recovered materials processing facility. 
(4)  To directly or indirectly dump, place or otherwise deposit any matter, including common household waste, onto the grounds surrounding a county dumpster. 
(5)  Who gathers or collects common household waste for compensation or remuneration of any kind to dump, place or otherwise deposit such common household waste into a county dumpster. 
(Ord. No. O-3-95, § 1.06, 7-6-1995) 
Sec. 46-135. - Prima facie evidence. 
It shall be prima facie evidence that the garbage or waste was dumped, placed or deposited by the person whose name appears on documents, correspondence or other writing discovered within the garbage or waste. 
(Ord. No. O-3-95, § 1.07, 7-6-1995) 
Sec. 46-136. - Penalty. 
Jurisdiction over offenses under this article shall be in the county magistrate court. Any person violating the terms of this article may be punished by a fine as provided in section 1-19, for each offense. Any sentence may also include restitution to the county or to any other appropriate person or entity. 
(Ord. No. O-3-95, § 1.08, 7-6-1995) 
Chapter 49 - SUBDIVISIONS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 49-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Subdivision means any division of a tract or parcel of land into five (5) or more lots, building sites, mobile home sites, or other divisions, for the purpose, whether immediate or future, of sale, legacy, or building development, and includes any multifamily residential development, re-subdivision and, where appropriate to the context, relates to the process of subdividing or to the land or area subdivided, provided, however, that the following are not included within this definition: 
(a)  The combination or recombination of previously platted lots or portions thereof where the total number of lots is not increased and the resultant lots conform to the standards of these rules; 
(b)  The division of land into parcels, all of which are three (3) acres or more where no new street is provided, the extension of public sewer and water lines is not required, and where said three-acre tracts front on existing roads approved and adopted by the county commission; and 
(c)  The division of land among heirs. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 1, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-2. - Applicability. 
This article applies to any subdivision of property made after the adoption of this article. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 2, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-3. - Plat approval required. 
From and after the passage of this article, it shall be unlawful to record a plat of land subdivision in the office of the Dade County Superior Court Clerk unless the plat shall have the approval of the Dade County Code Enforcement Officer inscribed thereon. Further, it shall be unlawful to transfer, sell, offer for or agree to sell, lease, rent, begin construction or otherwise begin the physical development of a lot or lots in a subdivision unless a plat of land subdivision has been given approval by the Dade County Code Enforcement Officer. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 3, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-4. - Essential services required. 
In order that prospective lot purchasers may get useable products and new subdivisions may be an asset rather than a liability to the community, the sub-divider shall install or construct the improvements as required by law, including but not limited to those described below, prior to having released financial assurances which guarantee installation of required improvements. All required improvements shall be constructed in accordance with the standards set forth in applicable federal, state, and county statutes, ordinances, rules, and regulations, including but not limited to the following: 
(a)  Utilities. Placement of all utility lines underground is encouraged. When the lines of electrical, telephone, other communications, natural gas or other utility providers are located in a street right-of-way, the main trunk lines shall be located outside the portion of the street to be surfaced to prevent having to cut into the paved surface to serve abutting properties. 
(b)  Water supply. The distribution system shall be designed and constructed to meet or exceed the federal and state minimum standards adopted for water systems, including those which may be utilized for fire protection. The location and placement of all fire hydrants shall be in accordance with federal, state, and county statutes, ordinances, rules and regulations. 
(c)  Sanitary sewer. Sanitary sewers or other sewage disposal systems shall be installed according to the plans and specifications approved by the Dade County Board of Health, and all other federal, state, county, statutes, ordinances, rules and regulations. When the sewer line is located in a street right-of-way and it will be necessary to cut into the street surface to serve abutting lots, a connection shall be stubbed out to the property line to serve each lot prior to surfacing the street. 
(d)  Curb and gutters. Curbs or gutters where required shall be installed in accordance with plans and specifications prepared by an engineer, and approved by the county road superintendent. 
(e)  Streets. Every lot in the subdivision shall front on a street constructed in accordance with the county road ordinance that is served by a public street or highway. No street shall dead-end without a permanent cul-de-sac with at least a one hundred twenty-foot diameter. No street crossing a dam shall be accepted by the county as a county road. 
(f)  Utilities in streets. All water mains, sanitary sewers and laterals, utilities, and storm sewers shall be installed as necessary to prevent the future cutting of the pavement of any street, sidewalk or other required pavement. 
(g)  Street pattern. All subdivisions shall provide for safe, all-weather, and convenient access and circulation by emergency and other vehicles. Georgia Department of Education policy is to locate school bus stops within one-quarter (¼) mile (1,320 feet) of every residence and that the street layout does not require buses to back up. This may be accomplished by a street layout that employs one (1) or more of the following techniques: (a) looped street patterns; (b) turnarounds designed for school buses (and fire trucks) not more than one thousand (1,000) feet apart in long streets or cul-de-sacs; (c) cul-de-sac turnarounds meeting the requirements of the road ordinance. 
(h)  Erosion and Sedimentation Control Plan approval. The development of land usually necessitates some degree of grading, excavating or the removal of topsoil, trees, and vegetation. Such soil disturbance shall be performed only in compliance with federal, state, and county statutes, ordinances, rules, and regulations. 
(i)  Storm drainage. An adequate drainage system, including necessary swales, open ditches, pipes, culverts, storm sewers, intersectional drains, drop inlets, bridges and other necessary appurtenances shall be installed by the sub-divider according to plans and specifications in compliance with federal, state, and county statutes, ordinances, rules, and regulations. 
(j)  Street name signs. Street name signs shall be installed at all intersections within a subdivision and in accordance with state and county statutes, ordinances, rules, and regulations. 
(k)  Subdivision entrances. The entrances, driveways, or curb cuts on all state and county roads shall comply with all federal, state, and county statutes, ordinances, rules, and regulations. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 4, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-5. - Plat review and approval procedure. 
The prospective sub-divider is strongly encouraged to meet early and informally with the code enforcement official to obtain advice and assistance before conducting any land disturbance or preparing the preliminary plat. This will enable the sub-divider to become familiar with federal, state, and county standards for subdividing land and constructing improvements, detailed procedures for plat approval, and the conditions under which the county will accept new public roads and utilities. 
The procedure for approval of a subdivision plat consists of two (2) separate steps. The initial step is the preparation and submission to the code enforcement officer, prior to making any street improvements or installations of utilities, of a preliminary plat of the proposed subdivision prepared by a Georgia registered surveyor in a form acceptable to the county. 
The second step is submission of a final plat, together with the required certificates, as the preliminary plat or portions of it are constructed or included in the letter of credit. The final plat shall conform substantially to the preliminary plat as approved, and shall be in a form acceptable to the code enforcement officer. This final plat, upon approval, shall be recorded as the official plat of record in the office of the clerk of the superior court of Dade County within ten (10) days of its signing by the code enforcement officer. 
Preliminary plat requirements. The preliminary plat for all subdivisions shall meet the minimum standards of design and the general requirements set forth in the State of Georgia Department of Human Resources Regulations for Subdivision and Mobile Home Parks and the Department's Manual for On-Site Sewage Management Systems, as may be amended by the State of Georgia from time to time. Additionally, the Preliminary Plat shall include a plat of the subdivision drawn at a scale of not more than one (1) inch equals one hundred (100) feet, and showing the following: 
(a)  Street plan, including the location of all existing and proposed streets within the subdivision and adjacent to it; widths and purpose of existing and proposed rights-of-way and easements; identification of right-of-way location and width for any street which is considered part of the sketch thoroughfare plan; proposed street names subject to approval; and typical cross section of proposed streets, showing natural and finished grades; 
(b)  Feasible connections to existing or proposed utility systems and any proposed improvements requested of the county; 
(c)  Plans of all proposed utility layouts and easement, including but not limited to a preliminary plan of sanitary sewage systems, with grade, pipe size and points of discharge; preliminary plan of the water supply system, with pipe sizes and location of hydrants; preliminary plan of the storm sewer system, with grade, pipe sizes and location of outlets; and preliminary plan of the location of all communication systems; preliminary plan for gas and electricity supply systems; and 
(d)  Location and dimension of land to be dedicated or reserved for parks, open space or other public use. 
Within forty-five (45) days after the submission of the preliminary plat, the code enforcement office shall review the plat with pertinent utilities, county departments, and other governmental entities, and indicate its approval, disapproval, or approval subject to any required modifications. If the plat is disapproved or is approved subject to modifications, the reasons for such disapproval of the required modifications shall be indicated in writing on two (2) copies of the plat. 
One (1) copy of the preliminary plat shall be retained in the code enforcement officer's files, and one (1) copy shall be returned to the sub-divider at the time of approval or disapproval. 
Final plat requirements. The final plat shall comply with all of the requirements for the preliminary plat, and any modifications thereto and in addition shall include: 
(a)  Final as-built survey data on property lines, easements, streets, lots, storm sewer system, utilities, and other improvements; 
(b)  Certifications evidencing ownership of the subject property, satisfactory provision of financial assurances sufficient to assure completion of all required improvements, and accuracy of the survey and plat and placement of all required monuments, health department approval, and other required information. 
The applicant shall submit five (5) copies together with any street profiles or other plans which may be required by the code enforcement officer. When the plat has been approved by the county, one (1) copy shall be submitted for filing with the clerk of the superior court within ten (10) days as the official plat of record. One (1) copy containing all required certifications shall be retained by the county, and one (1) copy shall be given to the sub-divider for his records. The acceptance of the final plat does not constitute acceptance of sub-divider's streets or roads as a county road. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 5, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-6. - Financial assurances required. 
Following the approval of the preliminary plat, but prior to approval of the final plat, the sub-divider shall obtain all permits; construct and install all public improvements and lot improvements as required by federal, state, or county statutes, ordinances, rules, and regulations; request approval of the subdivision plat from the codes enforcement officer; and request county acceptance of any public improvements, free and clear of all liens and encumbrances on the dedicated property and public improvements. 
In lieu of the completion of required improvements prior to the final approval of a plat, the county may accept cash, a certified check, or an irrevocable letter of credit, in such an aggregate amount as is estimated by the county to be the total cost of the construction and installation of all public improvement which are the responsibility of the sub-divider. Any certified check or letter of credit shall be made payable to Dade County, with a bank satisfactory to Dade County, and shall contain conditions and terms providing for and securing to the county the satisfactory construction, installation, and dedication of the incomplete portion of the required improvements. 
If the construction, repair, or replacement of any improvements or facilities for which the financial assurance is provided is not completed within one (1) month after substantial completion of any building or structures which said improvements or facilities are designed to serve, or within one (1) year after the date of recording the final plat, whichever is sooner, or if said construction, repair, or replacement is not in accordance with applicable standards, the county may proceed to construct, install or modify said improvements or facilities in accordance with the applicable specifications and requirements using the proceeds from such financial assurances to pay for such work. The financial assurance shall be released when the required improvement(s) is accepted and when the other construction, installation and dedication is completed. The form of the financial assurance is subject to approval by the county. 
After the furnishing of financial assurances to the satisfaction of the county, the sub-divider may proceed with the recording of lots, sale of lots, application for building permits, and application for county acceptance of streets and rights-of-way and other lands to be dedicated to the public. Nothing in this article shall constitute a guarantee by the county that the required improvements will be performed. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 6, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-7. - Private streets. 
(a)  Dade County may approve the construction of a private street within a subdivision. A private street is a street that is not accepted by the county as part of the county road system and is privately owned and maintained. Such streets or roads shall be constructed to the same standards and shall meet all other requirements with regard to road construction as is required for acceptance of such roads as public streets or roads. In addition, the developer shall: 
(1)  Provide the county with a written release of maintenance agreement, acceptable to the county manager, releasing the county from responsibility for present or future maintenance and upkeep of the roadway; 
(2)  Erect a sign indicating the existence of a private street at the intersection of each public street with a private street; 
(3)  Include a disclosure statement on all sales agreements, deeds and plats relating to the subdivision or its lots indicating that the street or road is a private street, that the county has no responsibility for its maintenance or upkeep, the nature of the ownership of the street and responsibility for its maintenance and upkeep, and the rights of purchasers of lots in the subdivision to enforce such provisions. 
(b)  Such private streets shall be platted and deeded to a responsible association or entity, such as a homeowners' association. Dade County may require, as a condition to approval of a private street or road: 
(1)  That the sub-divider provides a specific maintenance plan or financial guarantee of proper maintenance and repair; 
(2)  Access easements in favor of the county and its various departments and agencies; or 
(3)  Such other concessions as are deemed appropriate for the public good and the benefit of the lot owners. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 7, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-8. - Common areas. 
All common areas within the subdivision, including, but not limited to, private streets or roads, retention or detention ponds, playgrounds, clubhouses, pools and the like, shall be conveyed to a responsible association or entity, such as a homeowners' association, which has the responsibility for maintenance and upkeep of the common area. The county shall have no liability with regard to or responsibility for the maintenance or repair of such common areas. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 8, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-9. - Access required. 
A subdivision shall not be approved in a location where the existing roads providing primary access are inadequate to serve the additional traffic generated by the development. Where existing roads are inadequate to serve the additional traffic, the county shall require paved access to the subdivision from an existing paved state or county road. If the ditches on existing county roads are to be used for drainage from the subdivision, the developer shall re-grade such ditches and provide an all-weather drainage outlet. All re-grading and drainage outlets shall be approved by the board of commissioners or its authorized representatives. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 9, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-10. - Variances; appeals of decisions of the code enforcement officer. 
(a)  Variances. The code enforcement officer may authorize upon appeal in specific cases such variance from the terms of the article as will not be contrary to the public interest where, owning to special conditions, a literal enforcement of the provisions of the article will, in an individual case, result in practical difficulty or unnecessary hardship, so that the spirit of the article shall be observed, public safety and welfare secured, and substantial justice done. Such variance may be granted in such individual case of unnecessary hardship and shall be set forth in writing by the code enforcement officer. In determining whether or not to grant a variance, the code enforcement officer shall consider, along with other relevant facts, whether there are extraordinary and exceptional conditions pertaining to the particular piece of property in question because of its size, shape or topography; whether the application of this article to this particular piece of property would create an unnecessary hardship; whether such conditions are peculiar to the particular piece of property involved; and whether relief, if granted, would not cause substantial detriment to the public good or impair the purposes and intent of this article. 
(b)  Appeals. Decisions made by the code enforcement officer pursuant to this article may be appealed to the Dade County Board of Commissioners. Appeals shall be submitted in writing to the county clerk within seven (7) calendar days of the decision of the code enforcement officer. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 10, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-11. - Violation; penalties. 
Any violation of the provisions of this article shall constitute a misdemeanor and shall be punishable by penalties and costs as set forth in § 1-19 of the county code of ordinances. In the event any provision of the article has been violated or is being violated, in addition to other remedies, the county may institute an injunction, mandamus, or other appropriate action or proceeding to correct or stop such violation, and may refuse to issue any and all permitting relating to such sub-dividing of land, including building permits thereon, until such violations are corrected. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 11, 11-19-2009) 
Sec. 49-12. - Enforcement of other laws not limited; severability; effective date. 
(a)  This article shall not limit the authority of any state, county, or other governmental agency to enforce any other applicable laws, rules, regulations, or ordinances. 
(b)  In the event any section, subsection, sentence, clause, or phrase of this article is declared or adjudged to be unconstitutional, or otherwise contrary to law, such adjudication shall in no manner affect any other section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase, and shall remain in full force and effect as if the section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase so declared or adjudged invalid or unconstitutional was not originally a part hereof. 
(c)  This article shall become effective immediately upon its adoption, and all ordinances in conflict with this article are repealed to the extent of the conflict. 
(Ord. No. 11-19-09, § 12, 11-19-2009) 
Chapter 50 - TAXATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Any resolution or ordinance promising or guaranteeing the payment of money for the county or authorizing the issuance of any bonds of the county or any evidence of the county's indebtedness saved from repeal, § 1-13(2); any appropriation resolution or ordinance saved from repeal, § 1-13(7); any resolution or ordinance providing for local improvements and assessing taxes for such local improvements saved from repeal, § 1-13(9); any resolution or ordinance levying or imposing taxes not included in this Code saved from repeal, § 1-13(14); administration, ch. 2; finance, § 2-251 et seq. 
State Law reference— Local government budgets and audits, O.C.G.A. § 36-81-1 et seq.; accounting for public funds, O.C.G.A. § 45-8-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 50-1. - Gross premiums tax. 
In accordance with O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2, there is levied for the year 1984, and for each year thereafter, an annual tax upon each insurer doing business within the unincorporated area of the county, in an amount equal to two and one-half percent (2½%) of the gross direct premiums received during the calendar year on all insurance, other than life insurance, as defined in O.C.G.A. § 33-3-5(2), (3), (4) and (5). The term "gross direct premiums" shall mean gross direct premiums as used in O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2(a). 
(Res. of 9-27-1983, § 1) 
State Law reference— Local tax on other than life insurance companies, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2; general assembly authorized to provide for taxation of insurance companies based on gross direct premiums received from insurance policies within the unincorporated areas of counties, Ga. Const. art. IX, § IV, ¶ I(c). 
Sec. 50-2. - State cable and video service franchise fees. 
The county, by and through its Board of Commissioners, shall hereby require collection of franchise fees at the rate of five percent (5%) of annual gross revenues generated by any cable or video service provider providing cable or video services within the unincorporated areas of the county pursuant to a state franchise or the maximum that may be subsequently allowed by law. 
(Res. No. R-43-14, 8-7-2014) 
State Law reference— Consumer Choice for Television Act, O.C.G.A. tit. 36, ch. 76. 
Secs. 50-3—50-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - FINANCIAL INSTITUTIONS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Local depository financial institutions business license tax, O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93. 

Sec. 50-31. - Business license tax on financial institutions. 
In accordance with O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93, there is levied for the year 1984, and for each year thereafter, an annual business license tax upon all depository financial institutions located within the county, at a rate of one-fourth percent (¼%) of the gross receipts of such depository financial institutions. The term "gross receipts" shall mean gross receipts as defined in O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93. The term "depository financial institutions" shall mean state and national banks, state building and loan associations and federal savings and loan associations. 
(Res. of 9-30-1983, § 1) 
Sec. 50-32. - Minimum business license tax. 
The minimum annual amount of business license tax due from any depository financial institution pursuant to section 50-31 shall be one thousand dollars ($1,000.00). 
(Res. of 9-30-1983, § 2) 
Sec. 50-33. - Filing of return. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93(c), each depository financial institution subject to the business license tax shall file a return of its gross receipts with the sole commissioner of the county on March 1 of the year following the year in which such gross receipts are measured. Such return shall be in the manner and in the form prescribed by the commissioner of the department of revenue based on the allocation method set forth in O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93(d). The sole commissioner of the county shall assess and collect the tax levied in this article based upon the information provided in such return. 
(Res. of 9-30-1983, § 3) 
Sec. 50-34. - Due date of taxes. 
Taxes levied pursuant to this article shall be due no later than thirty (30) days after filing of the return prescribed by section 50-33 unless extended by the sole commissioner of the county. 
(Res. of 9-30-1983, § 4) 
Secs. 50-35—50-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - ENERGY EXCISE TAX 

Sec. 50-51. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Dealer. Shall have the meaning as provided in O.C.G.A. § 48-13-110. 
Local sales and use tax. Shall have the meaning as provided in O.C.G.A. § 48-13-110. 
Purchaser. Shall have the meaning as provided in O.C.G.A. § 48-13-110. 
(Ord. No. 12-06-12, § 1, 12-6-2012) 
Sec. 50-52. - Imposition; rate; remitting; recovery; liabilities. 
In accordance with the provisions of O.C.G.A. §§ 48-13-110 et seq., there is imposed within the territorial limits of the special district created pursuant to O.C.G.A § 48-13-111, an excise tax on the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy when such sale, use, storage, or consumption would have constituted a taxable event for purposes of sales and use tax under O.C.G.A. §§ 48-8-1 et seq. but for the exemption in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2. 
(Ord. No. 12-06-12, § 2, 12-6-2012) 
Sec. 50-53. - Excise tax rate; phase-in. 
(a)  Such excise tax shall be levied and collected by the governing authority of the county pursuant to O.C.G.A. §§ 48-13-112 and 48-13-114 and as provided in this section. 
(b)  Except as otherwise provided in this section, the rate of such excise tax shall be phased in over a four-year period as follows: 
(1)  For the period commencing January 1, 2013, and concluding at the last moment of December 31, 2013, such excise tax shall be at a rate equivalent to twenty-five percent (25%) of the total amount of local sales and use tax in effect in such special district that would be collected on the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy but for the exemption in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2; 
(2)  For the period commencing January 1, 2014, and concluding at the last moment of December 31, 2014, such excise tax shall be at a rate equivalent to fifty percent (50%) of the total amount of local sales and use tax in effect in such special district that would be collected on the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy but for the exemption in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2; 
(3)  For the period commencing January 1, 2015, and concluding at the last moment of December 31, 2015, such excise tax shall be at a rate equivalent to seventy-five percent (75%) of the total amount of local sales and use tax in effect in such special district that would be collected on the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy but for the exemption in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2; and 
(4)  On or after January 1, 2016, such excise tax shall be at a rate equivalent to one hundred percent (100%) of the total amount of local sales and use tax in effect in such special district that would be collected on the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy but for the exemption in O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2. 
(c)  In accordance with O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3.2 (c)(4), if a project of regional significance under O.C.G.A. § 48-8-3(92) is started in the special district, it shall not be subject to the phase-in period contained in subsection (b)(1),(2), and (3) of this section, and the sale, use, storage, or consumption of energy in connection therewith shall be subject to the rate specified in subsection (b)(4) of this section notwithstanding the January 1, 2016 limitation in that paragraph (b)(4). 
(d)  Following such initial imposition during the phase-in time period, on or after January 1, 2016, the rate of the excise tax levied and collected by the governing authority of the county shall be directed by O.C.G.A. § 48-13-112(d). 
(1)  Such rate shall be controlled by the maximum amount of local sales and use tax in effect in the special district, but in no event more than two percent (2%), excepting that the rate would be no more than three percent (3%) should the city levy an optional water and sewer tax.
